1
Chapter 1. Introduction
1.1. Confidentiality
The present manual is only for the insight of persons participating directly to the project. Any
forwarding of this documentation, in particular to contract partners outside of the BMW Group,
must be agreed with the appropriate responsible project leader and must comply with the
regulations and specifications of the confidentiality agreement of the development contract.
1.2. Purpose
This document corresponds to E-Sys user manual, describing all available functionalities (GUI and
batch), including the process of programming ECUs with E-Sys. Specifically for the use case of
programming, it is assumed that valid software units (SWEs) have already been created with the
SWE-Generator. The handling of the SWE-Generator is described in [SWEGEN].

Chapter 2. Basics
2.1. Installation
From version 22.06.XX on, E-Sys is always installed under C:\EC-Apps\E-Sys directory. This is
because a separate Windows firewall rule was created for this path to allow HTTP flashing. If the
installation directory will be manually renamed, we cannot guarantee that the HTTP flash process
will run smoothly!
2.2. Programming flow
The following steps are necessary to program an ECU with E-Sys:
1. Creating a PDX component container
a. Loading a PDX template
b. Creating ECU variants and adding ECU software (bootloader, application, coding data) in the
shape of software units (SWEs)
c. Adding configuration files (mapping, sequence, …)
d. Saving the component container
2. Importing the component container into PSdZ
3. Creating a transaction list (TAL) that defines the actions to be performed by the programming
system
4. Connecting to the ECU
5. Executing the TAL (programming the software image to the ECU)
2.3. Settings
All program and user settings can be modified in the menu „Options ᾆ Settings“. System specific
information will be saved in the file
<E-Sys_installation>\config\Esys.properties
User specific settings will be saved in
C:\Documents and Settings\<login>\Esys\EsysUser.properties
The settings will be described in the following sections.
It is also possible to modify these user settings directly in the previously defined files (these changes
must be done carefully). For example, users that use E-Sys in batch mode do not have a graphical
interface that allows them to change these properties. For such use cases, System properties
describes the properties that can be changed by the user.
5
2.3.1. Program
Program settings
Global settings are specified in the tab "Program", the following settings can be made:
• Directories: Defines where the NCD-Data (NCD-Root), the E-Sys generated data including the ESys folder structure (Data) as well as the directory where the folder psdzdata is located which
included all imported PDX-container are saved. The directory where the E-Sys relevant data is
stored (e.g. FA, Log, TAL, SVT, …) will be referred to <E-Sys_data>. For the directory, that is set at
„PSdZ-Data“ is important, that there is just one psdzdata folder located. In these folders are the
ODX date be stored.
• Language: Switches the E-Sys GUI from German to English and vice versa.
• Logging: Sets the log level for E-Sys. Log files are automatically created in the folder <ESys_data>/Logs at system start with the name pattern E-Sys_yyyymmdd_hhmmss.log (e.g. ESys_20090112_143821.log). Old log files can be deleted at system start by activating the provided
checkbox.
Directories
Data Data directory (Default: C:\Data)
PSdZ-Data PSdZ-Data directory (Default: C:\Data)
NCD-Root NCD-Root directory (Default: C:\Data\CAF\NCD)
6
• In the Data directory, E-Sys stores all relevant data (Log, TAL, executedTAL, SVT, FA, etc.).
• For PSdZ-Data, a directory must be entered in which the psdzdata directory is to be created.
This is where the contents of the imported containers are stored.
• For NCD-Root, a directory must be entered in which the subdirectories "unsigned", "signed" and
"default" (delivery state) should be created. This directory stores the net encoding data used for
encoding.
Language
German Set to German language
English Set to English language
Select the language used to represent E-Sys.
Logging
Log-Level Setting of log levels
Delete old log files automatically during restart During start all old log files are deleted
This setting allows the user to control the E-Sys log level.
The default setting is "DEEP_TRACE".
For analysis of errors (programming, coding or e-sys errors), the log level "DEEP_TRACE" is
mandatory.
Log level Description
OFF The log does not include any additional log output.
WARN The log also includes WARN editions
INFO The log also includes INFO and WARN outputs
FINE The log also includes FINE, INFO and WARN outputs
DEBUG The log also includes DEBUG, FINE, INFO and WARN outputs
TRACE The log also includes TRACE, DEBUG, FINE, INFO and WARN outputs
DEEP_TRACE The log also includes DEEP_TRACE, TRACE, DEBUG, FINE, INFO and WARN
outputs
ProDiaS Log-Level
Base settings Sets the global log settings for ProDiaS
Advanced settings Sets the log setting for each of ProDias action
category
This setting allows the user to control the ProDiaS log level.
The default setting is "INFO".
7
Each category has four log levels.
The user can set the log level for individual categories or for the global project.
Log level Description
INFO The log also includes INFO and WARN outputs
TRACE The log also includes TRACE, INFO and WARN outputs
WARN The log also includes WARN editions
ERROR The log also includes TRACE, INFO, WARN and ERROR outputs

Car E-Sys is used for programming/coding car

SOURCE_DATE_EPOCH:
The environment variable SOURCE_DATE_EPOCH is entered in the META data when the PDX
containers are created.
If this value is not set, the current system time is used.
If the value is set, the contents of the environment variable SOURCE_DATE_EPOCH is used.
For more information, see: https://reproducible-builds.org/docs/timestamps/.
The user is responsible for ensuring that the variable contains the correct value.
If the variable is not set or does not contain a valid timestamp, the current system time is used.
E-Sys Mode:
Selection of control units should be treated with cars or motorcycle routines.
Especially at VCM, different routines are available here.

2.3.6. Proxy
This tab allows to define and set a proxy-server. This proxy, if active, is used for the communication
to external systems (e.g. SWL-Cockpit, CBB, SWL-Sec2, SFA-Backend). It can be configured that the
active proxy isn´t to be used if E-Sys is communicating with one of the Proxy-Blacklist URLs. It the
configured Proxy requires an authorisation the popup where you can enter your credentials
appease if the proxy is used for the first time during the E-Sys session. The proxy-credential are
only remembered for the time of the current session by E-Sys.
Proxy settings

edited if the check mark is set here.

for proxy server. The prompt for entering the
login data for proxy does not appear until a
backend interface is called up.

In the txt-file, the URLs may only be entered in one line and only separated with a semicolon ;. ESys does not support another formats of the URLs. Example: https://www.google1.de;https://
www.bmwgroup.com;https://www.bing2.com
Add:
Only one URL may be added at a time. 
Multiple entries (separated with semicolon ";") are invalid.

Chapter 3. Creating and importing a PDX
component container
The following chapter describes the creation of a PDX component container based on a PDX
template and its import into the PSdZ programming system.
3.1. Loading the PDX template
To be able to create a component container, the current PDX template must first be loaded in the
Data Handling → PDX Charger module.
 The current PDX template can be obtained via SWL-Cockpit.
When loading a PDX, E-Sys will show an option asking if the user wants to save the contents of the
PDX file after extraction. If the Yes option is selected, then the extracted PDX folder will be persisted
after E-Sys is closed. This will lead to faster loading when this PDX is reloaded. If the No option is
selected, then extracted folder will be deleted when E-Sys is closed.
Save previously extracted PDX option pane
If an extracted folder exists in the same directory as the PDX, a new pane will appear asking if the
previously extracted folder should be used. If the Yes option is selected, the folder’s contents will be
read and loaded into E-Sys. If the option is selected, the extracted folder will be deleted and the PDX
contents will be extracted.
PDX Charger with opened PDX template
26
3.2. Assignment of main series
Since E-Sys 3.15, the series associations (BRV) for which a PDX container is to be valid can be
selected in the PDX-Charger. The main series available for selection are determined in each case by
the PDX template used. The selection is made in a separate dialog that can be opened by pressing
the "Edit" button (see red marking):
Selection of the main series
27
3.3. Adding ECU software
In the folder structure of the PDX template, new ECU variants can be created via the context menu
by right-clicking on the PDX container element. The ECU can be an ECU or SMAC variant.
A new ECU variant must first be assigned to a base variant. This is done by selecting the desired
base variant from the drop-down box of the element with the same name. The name can then be
defined for the new ECU variant. When defining the name, it is only important to ensure that the
name ends with the suffix "EV".
28
In the case of Smart Actuators (SMAC) there is no base variant and the SMAC name is initially
arbitrary. As soon as a BTLD file is added, the name must correspond to a matching EE component
name.
Finally, below the base variant, the respective software units can be added by right-clicking on the
SWE element and selecting Add. The corresponding SWE files are then selected via a file dialog.
 Only SWEs in BSW format can be added to the container.
They are automatically extracted and processed during import.
To an ECU exactly one base variant can be assigned. And to every base variant you can specify
bootloaderID and diagnostic address. Furthermore, it’s possible to deactivate a base variant.
ECUs are displayed with blue letters if of L4 and with black letters if it is an L6 ECU.
The container’s file versions are displayed in the lower window. Other than the display in the above
window (i.e. swfl_11111114) the file version gets displayed, too (swfl_11111114_001_001_002). For
SWE files it is possible to delete single file versions, but only if 2 SWE file versions for the same
identifier exist.
Already existing elements of the upper parts can be removed by context menu.
29
3.3.1. Coding Application Files (CAF)
The Coding Application Files (CAFs) required for coding are not hooked into the template at the ECU
variant, but below the CAF element. They are therefore not assigned to any ECU variant. The same
applies to the SVT files, which describe the target state of the component. They can be added to the
SVT element. All other configuration files, for example the mapping files for the transfer control
devices or the SWESEQ file (see Setting the programming order) for controlling the programming
sequence are added below the Config element.
3.4. Adding BLUP/FLUP files and BLUMap
Bootloader updaters of process classes BLUP/FLUP are inserted in the ECU variant below SWE in
the same way as conventional bootloader SWEs of process class BTLD:
Adding a BLUP to the component container
30
The selection of the files is done as usual in a file dialog.
If an ECU variant (in our example HSR_EV) contains at least one SWE of the process class BLUP or
FLUP, the associated BLUMap file can be added via the context menu of the base variant:
Adding a BLUMap file to the PDX container
The selection of the BLUMap file is again done via a file dialog. After selection, the name for the
BLUMap file can be changed. The naming convention for the BLUMap files is blumap_<base variant
name>_<EE component name>.xml.
If the BLUMap file was added to the container, the file appears in the tree structure of the PDXCharger below Config/blumaps, not below the ECU variant. The fact that a BLUMap has been stored
in the container for an ECU variant is indicated by the node "Bootloader map available: yes" below
the ECU variant.
Display of the BLUMap in the PDX-Charger
31
When importing the PDX container, the BLUP/FLUP-SWEs are stored in the psdzdata\swe\blup or
psdzdata\swe\flup directory, the BLUMap in the
psdzdata\mainseries\<BRV>\<project>\mapping\blumaps directory.
3.5. Adding user documents
By adding user documents the developer has the possibility to distribute also non-ODX content via
the component container (TAL, instructions, etc.). The documents are added via the context menu
of the DOC node. The component container must be saved before inserting the documents.
Adding user documentation to the PDX container
The added files are stored in the container in a ZIP archive with the name <component name>_Doku
32
.zip and listed in the PDX-Charger below DOC:
User documentation in the PDX container
The maximum size of the ZIP archive is limited to 1MB by default but can be adjusted under
Options → Settings → ODX (see Settings).
3.6. Setting the programming order
By including a sequence file in the PDX container it is possible to specify a programming sequence
for the software units of an ECU. The file must respect the naming convention sweseq_<BootloaderID>.xml.xxx_yy_zzz, where <Bootloader-ID> is the eight-digit bootloader SGBM ID of the ECU, for
example sweseq_01020304.xml.001_002_003 for the bootloader of the SC template. It is added to
the PDX container below the Config node.
Loaded SWESEQ file in the SWESEQ-Editor
The above figure shows the SWESEQ editor (SWE sequences), which can be used to create SWESEQ
files in E-Sys.
33
In the previous example image, the software unit 11121314 has to be programmed before software
units 21222324, 31323334 and 41424344 on an ECU with standard core template (bootloader ID
01020304, diagnostic address 0x7E, base variant EVALBOARD). The software units 21222324,
31323334 and 41424344 can be programmed in any sequence preferred by the programming
system.
Only dependencies for programming can be specified ("A must be programmed before B and C"), not
a fixed programming sequence. The programming system then determines a possible programming
sequence from the specified dependencies at runtime.

If the SWESEQ file contains cyclic dependencies ("A before B" and "B before A"),
programming will be aborted.
For each dependency a new EcuDependencies section has to be created within the SWESEQ file.
Within such a section the following elements have to be filled:
• BootloaderId: The bootloader ID of the designated ECU
• BaseVariant: The ECUs base variant (as listed in the PDX container)
• PhysicalOffset: The ECUs diagnostic address (hex)
• PreConditions: A list of SGBM-IDs of software units to be programmed before those listed in
Dependors.
• Dependors: A list of SGBM-IDs of software units to be programmed after those listed in
PreConditions.

SWESEQ files can also be used to specify an order among master (BTLD) and slave
bootloader (FLSL). If no dependency is specified between those the slave
bootloader (FLSL) will be programmed first. Structural dependencies (e.g. BTLD
before SWFL, SWFL before CAF) don’t need to be defined here. If the dependencies
specified by the user are in conflict with those elementary rules programming will
be aborted!
3.7. Saving the component container
When the container covers all desired ECU variants and configuration files it obviously must be
saved for further use. Use the “Save as” function for this purpose not to overwrite the underlying
template.
The chosen name is important, and it most comply with the following use-case and guidance.
When a PDX Component Container is imported into the PDX-Charger the name will be verified to
check if it is valid. The rules vary depending if the name structure is version 3 or older:
• If it is older the name structure will be the series, that is represented by 4 characters that can be
letters or digits.
◦ Then it is followed by an underscore and a combination of 1 to 8 characters that can be
digits, upper case letters or underscores.
34
• Optionally the user can use two underscores followed by a combination of 1 to 8 characters that
can be digits, upper case letters and underscore.
◦ Then this is followed by the version. The version is represented by three numbers of three
digits between 0 and 255 that are separated by underscores. It is terminated with a pdx
extension.
Example: F010_Example__Ex_12.001_020_223.pdx.
• For a PDX Component Container which version is 3 or above, the structure starts by a
combination of 1 to 8 characters that can be digits, upper case letters or underscores and then is
followed by two underscores and another combination of 1 to 8 characters that can be digits,
upper case letters or underscores.
◦ This is then followed by two underscores and a combination of 1 to 20 characters that can be
digits, upper case letters or underscores. Then it is followed by the version and the pdx
extension.
Naming convention:
<E/E Component>__<freetext>.<version>.pdx
E/E Component [A-Z0-9_]\{1,8}__[A-Z0-9_]\{1,8} E.g., ZBE__04
Free text [A-Z0-9_]\{1,20} E.g., F001
Version \d{3}_\d{3}_\d{3} E.g., 003_004_000
Example of a valid component container name: ZBE__04__F001.003_004_000.pdx
Each version part must be in the range [0-255]. Any other value will not be allowed.
For example, ZBE__04__F001.003_004_256.pdx is an invalid component container name.
3.8. ODX-Checker
After saving, the container can be checked using the ODX checker, for formal correctness. The rules
required by the ODX checker are copied to the C:\Data\Rules directory during the E-Sys installation
in the current version. If more current checker rules are provided on the GIS, these must be
exchanged in the named directory by the user.
The result is presented in the "ODX checker messages" table.
35
Message details can be open with a double click on a line in the table.
36
The ODX checker rules could be stored in a directory. The path for the ODX checker rules is set in
the "Options / Settings…" menu in the "ODX" tab.

E-Sys contains ODX-Rules which have been developed exclusively for BMW as well
as ODX-Rules which have been purchased by BMW within the scope of the package
ASAM. If a user installs E-Sys on a hardware which is not owned by BMW AG or
any other affiliated company within in the BMW Group, the user shall:
1. Purchase a Licence for the ASAM-Rules (detailed information can be
obtained at http://www.asam.net) or
2. Delete the ASAM-Rules which can be found in the data directory (default:
C.\Data\Rules\asamrules.jar).
Otherwise the user commits a violation of third parties intellectual property (right
to licence).
3.9. Importing the component container into PSdZ
Before the contents of a PDX container can be used in E-Sys the container has to be imported into
the programming system by means of the button “Import into PSdZ”. When importing the container
a name differing from the container name can be specified as the project name under which the
container data is stored and displayed when connecting to a vehicle or ECU.

If a container is valid for more than one main series the PSdZ import creates a
project for each valid main series. If the first four characters of the project name
do not match the name of the main series, the name of the main series will be put
in front of the project name followed by an underscore.
37
Example: If a container valid for F001 and F010 is imported with the project name
“my_project”, the projects “F001_my_project” and “F010_my_project” will be
created.
During the import the data from the container is extracted and copied locally into the directory
<Esys_Data>/psdzdata for the use in E-Sys. The contents of <Esys_Data>/psdzdata can be viewed in ESys at any time in the file explorer and can also be edited.
File-Explorer view after ODX data import

Since files in the psdzdata/extLibs directory are used by the Java VM, this directory
cannot be deleted while E-Sys is running.
3.10. PDX-Update
By means of an update, it is possible to automatically bring an existing component container up to
the status of a newer PDX template. To do this, the component container must first be opened in
PDXCharger.
The update functionality is then triggered via the "Update" button.
38
The new PDXTemplate is selected and confirmed via a file dialog. E-Sys then replaces the templatespecific contents in the component container with those of the selected template; the ECU-specific
contents remain unchanged. The updated container can then be saved under the same name by
default or under a new name using File → Save as…

Upon starting the Module, the update button is still disabled. Only when a
container is loaded can the two buttons “Import into PSdZ” and “Update” be
selected.
The first container must be entered via the “…” Button on the 'old' container that the user wants to
update.
After pressing the update button, a file selection box pops up in which the user can specify the PDX
container with the new files.
E-Sys will now calculate the combined quantity of the two containers and display it. The modified
container can then be saved and imported into PSdZ.
3.11. PDX-Delete
To free up storage space and improve clarity, old containers can be removed. The "Delete container"
button is available for this purpose. To be able to delete a container, there must not be an active
connection.
Delete container
39
In the following selection dialog, a container to be deleted can be selected. After clicking the
"Delete" button, the security prompt must also be confirmed. After confirmation the container will
be removed.
The data that could not be assigned to a container is listed under "Undefined_Container".
Deleting a specific container

When deleting, the deletion process is limited exclusively to entries in the
subdirectories ..\psdzdata\swe and ..\psdzdata\mainseries.
Only the files that are not needed by any other PDX container are removed.
In exceptional cases, all containers can also be removed from the PSdZ directory. The "Delete all"
function is available for this purpose, which must also be confirmed via a security prompt.
Delete all containers
40
41
Chapter 4. Creating a TAL
In order to program an ECU, E-Sys needs a transaction list (TAL). A TAL can either be created
manually in the TAL-Editor, it can be calculated automatically in the module “TAL-Calculating”, or it
can be derived from an ECU variant in the PDX-Charger.

It is strongly recommended to calculate the TAL either from SVT-Actual and SVTTarget or from an ECU variant in the PDX-Charger (with SVT readout). This ensures
completeness and correctness of the TAL.
4.1. Manual creation in the TAL-Editor
In the TAL-Editor (section Editors & Viewers) an empty TAL can be created by the menu item File →
New or the corresponding item in the toolbar. An existing TAL can be edited by selecting File →
Open.
When creating a new TAL, one has to use different TAL-Lines with unique IDs for each ECU and
transaction class. Furthermore, each TAL-Line must be filled with the base variant name (not the
component name) and the diagnostic address (hex) of the designated ECU.
The remaining attributes (ExecutionStatus, FlashPreReqs, CodingPreReqs, …) do not have to be
altered.
Table 1. Base elements of a TAL-Line
TalLine Unique ID for each TAL-Line
BaseVariant Base variant of the ECU to be programmed as listed in the container
DiagAddress Diagnostic address of the ECU to be programmed (hex)
Elementary parts of each TAL-Line are the software units to be programmed. Those can be added
by appending a new transaction to a TAL-Line (by right-clicking the TAL-Line root element and
choosing New. It is important to pick the correct transaction category from the list e.g., SWDeploy
for programming application and data (process class SWFL). The following table displays the most
important transaction categories.
Table 2. Important transaction categories in the TAL
Transaction category Description
SWDeploy Programming application software and data (SWFL)
CDDeploy Programming coding data (CAFD)
BLFlash Programming a master or slave bootloader (BTLD/FLSL)
 If the software unit versions specified in the TAL do not match the versions of the
software unit file names programming will be aborted!
In addition, the InstalledEcuList_Actual/_Target must be filled with the ECUs (base variant and
diagnostic address) installed before/after TAL execution.
42

When creating a coding action (CD-Deploy) it is mandatory that the
ExpectedSGMIDs are listed completely. By complete, it is understood that all SBGM
IDs which are present on the ECU at the time must be listed before coding is
performed. In addition to the boot loaders (BTLD, FLSL), this also applies to the
software units (SWFL, SWFK) and the hardware units (HWEL, HWAP). The
background to this is that the BTLD below the ExpectedSGMIDs is a prerequisite
for the execution of an encoding and is checked for completeness by PSdZ. If
SGBMIDs are not listed in the TAL (under ExpectedSGMIDs) but are present on the
ECU, an error occurs which results in the coding not being able to be started.

4.2. Automatic TAL calculation
In the "TAL calculation" module, a TAL can be calculated by specifying a SVT actual and a SVT
target. The various options for determining a SVT actual or SVT target are explained in the
subchapters. The area of individual data recovery is discussed separately in a chapter: Recovering
individual data
As soon as a SVT actual and a SVT target are loaded, the difference is displayed in color in the left
window (blue = actual status, red = target status). In the "TAL-Filter" area, an additional filter can be
loaded that influences the calculation strategy of the TAL with regard to transaction classes and/or
control units to be handled.

Displaying of Default Entries in SVT
If a SVT is read out from the vehicle, it may not be possible to determine the current software status
(SVK = system installation identifier) of some ECUs. Such ECUs are included in the SVT as default
entries.
If default ECUs are contained in the SVT read out, this is announced to the user in a dialog and the
affected ECUs are marked accordingly in the SVT tree.
Displaying of Smart Actuators
If an SVT gets loaded or read, Smart Actuators are included which will get displayed inside the
related Smart Actuator Master Ecu Node. SVK’s from a Smart Actuator Master ECU are getting
highlighted by a red "S" instead of a dot.
SVT-Update
Within section 'SVT-Update' it is possible to update all versions of the SGBMIDs included in the
Target-SVT.
48
With button 'Update SVT' E-Sys will start a check for each SGBMID contained in the SVT and search
for versions of that SGBMID in the loaded PDA-Container.
If more than one version for a SGBMID is found in the PDX container, the user is asked to which
version the SVT should be updated.
For delta SWEs the target versions are also included as an option.
 Update will be aborted if container has only delta SWEs inside
Reading Vehicle Order and VIN
After reading the vehicle order the VIN will always be read too. The VIN will be shown in the
element ""FAList/FA/FZAuftrag/Header/Vinlong". The vehicle order and the VIN will be read from
the master ECU. If an error occurs they will be read from the backup ECU. In the status bar is
shown where the vehicle order and the VIN were actually read from.
Displaying TAL-Filter settings
If filter settings have been defined for the root element or any of the ECU elements in the SVT tree
view, these elements will be displayed with an additional filter symbol as soon as the TAL-Filter file
is loaded.
49
A detailed figure showing all filter settings of an element will be displayed via the context menu
entry 'Filter Settings'.

4.2.1.1. Loading the SVT Actual
The SVT Actual area offers four different ways to load SVTs.
SVT actual area
4.2.1.1.1. Read (ECU) incl. Smart Actuators
This button can be used to read an SVT actual with an active vehicle connection. Any Smart
Actuators that may be present are taken into account in the process.
4.2.1.1.2. Read (ECU) without Smart Actuators
The button offers the same function as described above, but Smart Actuators are not considered.
4.2.1.1.3. Reading (VCM)
The button reads the SVT actual from the VCM by means of the current vehicle connection.
4.2.1.1.4. Loading
The SVT-actual can be read in here with "Load" from a locally stored file.
4.2.1.2. Loading the SVT Target
There are also five ways to load an SVT target, but they are different from the SVT actual and are
described below.
SVT Target area
4.2.1.2.1. Loading from KIS
The desired SVT target can be calculated from KIS, if available, or also loaded from a file. When
51
calculating a SVT target from KIS, an FA must also be loaded and activated and, depending on the
calculation strategy, a construction stage or target I-step must be specified.

The calculation of a SVT target from KIS is only possible after importing an I-step
container. The available construction or target I-steps depend on the imported
container, the activated FA and the selected calculation strategy.
4.2.1.2.2. Loading from SVK preview
Access to the SWL Cockpit must exist for this function. The SVT target is downloaded after entering
the necessary data. The following entries are required:
• Via diagnostic address: The input of the I-step and diagnostic address is required.
• Via vehicle order: In the vehicle order area, a corresponding file must be loaded (see the
following figure), and it is also necessary to specify an I-step.
• Via vehicle order and BNTN variants: A vehicle order must also be loaded here. In addition to
the I-step, it is also necessary to enter a BNTN (onboard network subscriber) identifier.
Vehicle Order area
4.2.1.2.3. Generate by means of SVT update
To create an SVT target by means of an update, first the SVT actual is loaded in the SVT target area.
To update this SVT with the current versions from a component container, this is also loaded and
then the "Update SVT" button is pressed.
SVT update
After the update, a dialog with the update software units is displayed.

If the existing ECUs will be further used, the HW identifiers can be read from the
SVT actual (button "HW identifiers from SVTactual").
4.2.1.2.4. Load from file
The SVT-actual can be read in here with "Load" from a locally stored file.
52
4.2.1.2.5. Reading (VCM)
The button reads the SVT actual from the VCM of the currently connected vehicle.
4.2.1.3. Definition of a TAL filter
TAL filters are used in the automatic calculation of TALs and can influence the calculation strategy
with regard to the transaction classes and/or control units to be handled. Defining a TAL filter is
done in the "TALFILTER Editor" in the "Editors and Viewers" module. To create a valid TAL filter,
either an existing TAL filter can be loaded and modified, or a new TAL filter can be created based
on an SVT. Basically, the following filter options can be set for each transaction class of each
controller:
Table 3. Possible filter options for transactions
Option Description
Empty Execution of the transaction depends on differences in SVT actual and SVT target
(filter option is not listed in the TAL filter)
Allow Execution of the transaction depends on differences in SVT actual and SVT target
(filter option is listed in the TAL filter).
Prohibit Transaction is not executed (differences between SVT actual and SVT target are not
considered)
Force Transaction is executed (differences between SVT actual and SVT target are not
considered)
4.2.1.3.1. TALFILTER Editor
A generated or loaded TAL filter is displayed in the form of a table. The rows in the table represent
the individual ECUs that are potentially to be handled. The first row ("ecuAll") can be used to set a
global filter option for each transaction class. This global filter option is only considered during the
TAL calculation for those transactions whose filter option has not been explicitly defined at ECU
level (filter option = "empty"). The columns of the table have the following functions:
Table 4. Filter table description
Field/action Column Description
ID base (column 1) Identification of the ECU via the diagnostic address in the
hexadecimal format (decimal in square brackets).
Set All to… (column 2-5) Sets all TA classes of the corresponding controller to the filter
option of the corresponding column.
Specify… (column 6-7) Calls a separate dialog for defining filter options for the subtransaction classes of the swDeploy and ecuMirrorDeploy
transactions. The setting in the dialog sets the
swDeploy/ecuMirrorDeploy transaction to the "User defined" filter
option.
TA classes (column 8-18) Allows to explicitly edit a filter option of the respective TA class.
53
Creation of new TAL-Filter
There are two ways of creating a new filter file:
1. with File Menu
This will create an empty TAL-Filter with a content like the one shown below:
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8" standalone="yes"?>
<talfilter>
  <allEcu/>
</talfilter>
2. with SVT-File
After selecting an existing SVT file, a new TAL-Filter will be created when pressing button
'Calculation'. This TAL-Filter will contain empty entries for all ECUs defined in the SVT file.
Editing and Displaying TAL-Filter settings
As soon as a new TAL-Filter has been created or an existing filter has been loaded, its filter settings
will be displayed in a table structure:
54
For modifying the filter settings the user is offered several options:
1. 'Set All to…'
By using one of the buttons 'Empty', 'Allow', 'Prohibit' or 'Force' all Transaction Categories of
an ECU can be set to the same value.
Additionally, these four buttons located in the first row ('ecuAll'), will set all Transaction
Categories of all ECUs to the specified value.
2. 'Select Action'
Each Transaction category of every ECU can separately be set to one of the following action
values:
◦ Empty
◦ Allow
◦ Prohibit
◦ Force
Note: For Transaction category swDeploy it is possible to specify user defined settings for
swDeployTA, swDeleteTA and smacDeployOnMasterTA. Therefore, an additional action value
('user defined') will be available for that category. For Transaction category ecuMirrorDeploy it
is possible to specify user defined settings for ecuMirrorDeployTA and
smacEcuMirrorDeployOnMasterTA. Therefore, an additional action value ('user defined') will
also be available for that category.
3. 'swDeploy'
As mentioned before, it is possible to define additional filter settings for category swDeployTA,
swDeleteTA and smacSwDeployOnMasterTA. This can be done by opening an additional dialog
55
via the swDeploy button.
In the SWE Filter table, it is possible to add and remove filters at SWE ID level. These filters
override the global settings defined for SWE types.
Each table entry must contain 3 parameter: SWE type (e.g., SWFS, SWFL), SGBM numbers (multiple
values are allowed if separated with commas. e.g., 00000001,0000FFFF), and an action. In this
table, only the types that were previously selected can be added. Also, removing types at the top
can cause entries in the table to be removed (i.e. if there are entries for that type in the table).
4. ecuMirrorDeploy
As mentioned before, it is possible to define additional filter settings for category
ecuMirrorDeployTA and smacEcuMirrorDeployOnMasterTA.
This can be done by opening an additional dialog via the ecuMirrorDeploy button:
56
4.2.1.4. Start of the TAL calculation
As soon as a SVT actual and a SVT target have been loaded via one of the described options, a TAL
can now be generated via the "Calculate" button, which transfers the vehicle (or the ECU composite)
from the actual state to the target state.
Start of the TAL calculation
• If the checkbox "Include ECUs from SVTtarget only" is activated, only ECUs that are included in
the SVT target are considered in the calculation. ECUs that only appear in the SVT actual are
discarded in this mode.
• If the checkbox "with Mirror-Protocol" is activated, the TAL is created in such a way that the
tokens required for the mirror flash are automatically obtained from the backend during
processing.
The calculated TAL can then be saved, edited in the TAL editor, or processed directly. The "Save",
"Edit" and "Process" buttons are available for this purpose.
 The TAL calculation only works with an open connection.
4.2.2. Batch
Please refer to TAL calculation for the related batch commands.
If you’re interested in commands for reading SVT (with or without SmAcs), and/or other ECU data,
please refer to Read data.
57
4.3. Generation of a TAL in the PDX-Charger
If no KIS knowledge base is available, it may be useful to generate a TAL directly from the PDX
container data. TAL generation is possible both for the entire container and for individual ECU
variants. The generation of the TAL is triggered by the menu item "Generate TAL" in the context
menu of the ECU variant or the container root element.
TAL/SVT generation from a ECU variant.
All software units (SWE) that are directly assigned to the ECU variant are then automatically
transferred to the TAL. Depending on the nature of the container, it may then be necessary to
manually assign version numbers, diagnostic addresses, and CAF files to the ECU variant if this
assignment is not clearly possible from the ODX data.
Similarly, instead of a TAL, an SVT_target can also be calculated in PDX-Charger ("Generate SVT").
This SVT can then be used in the "TAL calculation" module to calculate a TAL based on a currently
read actual status (cf. chapter 4.2).

Advantage: Only the transactions that are actually necessary are generated in the
TAL.
To create a TAL/SVT in the PDX-Charger, a connection must be opened.

During TAL generation in the PDX-Charger, the InstalledECUList_Actual/Target of
the TAL is only filled automatically if a valid SVTactual can be read at this time,
otherwise the InstalledECUList_Actual/Target remains empty. In this case, the
installed ECUs must either be entered manually or the automatic filling during the
TAL processing must be activated.
If a PDX container contains a SmAc TAL generation won’t be available.
58
4.4. Creating a TAL with BLUP/FLUP
4.4.1. Automatic calculation in the "TAL calculation" module
The automatic TAL calculation, as described in Automatic TAL calculation also works with
BLUP/FLUP software units. The SVT_actual or SVT_target contains the actual/target bootloader of
the BTLD/FLSL process class. The information from the BLUMap is used to calculate the required
BLUP/FLUP-SWE for the TAL.

This method requires a connection to a project that contains valid BLUMaps for
the respective ECUs.
4.4.2. Automatic calculation in PDX-Charger

The calculation of a TAL with BLUP/FLUP or SmAc software units in PDX-Charger is
not possible. The actual status of the ECUs required for the calculation is not
available in the PDX-Charger.
4.4.3. Manual generation of the TAL with BLUP/FLUP
To manually insert a BLUP transaction into a TAL, proceed as follows:
1. Create a TAL line for the BLUP transaction and add a BLFlash transaction.
2. Delete the BLFlashTA entry BLFlash_BTLD_000000_001_000_000 created by default.
59
3. Create a new BLFlashTA from a file.
4. Select the desired BLUP file in the file dialog. A BLFlash transaction is generated that contains
both the SGBM ID of the BLUP (SgbmIdentifier) and the SGBM ID of the encapsulated BTLD
60
(ContainedBootloader).
61
Chapter 5. Connecting
5.1. Establish connection
Some functionalities of E-Sys, including programming or coding an ECU, need an established
connection with the PDX data or the vehicle. This is only possible with a PDX container successfully
imported into PSdZ. The connection dialogue can be opened by clicking the connection button in
the toolbar:
After the click on "establish connection" subsequent dialog is displayed:
The E-Sys connection dialogue is divided in three parts, i.e., “Target”, “Interface” and “Vehiclespecific parameter”. In the upper part of the “Target” section, the “TargetSelector” for the
connection can be chosen. The “TargetSelector” determines the ODX project (i.e., the data from an
imported container) you want to work with. In the “Interface” section the physical interface for the
connection can be defined. In the “Vehicle-specific parameter” section additional information about
the connected vehicle can be specified. The following sections explain the use of these settings
regarding the various connection types.
62
In the window "Target" you find all available projects and vehicle information. These could be
filtered by the main series. With the second filter selects either gateway or direct ECU connection.
After the selection of a target selector and vehicle info the connection could be established by
clicking on the "Connect" button.
If the connections was established successfully in the status bar you see the selected target.
The type of the connection could be chosen in the "Interface" part of the dialog:
• For a connection via bus the bus type and a interface must be selected.
• For a connection via gateway URL the appropriate URL with port must be defined.
• For a connection via ICOM/CAN the URL of the ICOM with the appropriate port must be defined.
• For a connection via ICOM/ETHERNET the URL of the ICOM with the appropriate port must be
defined. After an initial connection the port will be calculated from the base port taken from the
settings.
• For a connection via ICOM/VCPI the URL of the ICOM with the appropriate port must be defined.
You can choose between different offsets in the Connection tab in the Settings dialog.
TCP destination port (to ICOM_NEXT and VCPI) = base port + 10 x diagnostic address (dec) + offset
63
Offsets:
0: HSFZ 6801 - Destination port for master gateway behind VCPI
2: DoIP 13400 - Destination port for master gateway behind VCPI
3:DoIP over TLS 3496 - Destination port for TLS connections to the master gateway behind
the VCPI
• For a connection via VIN a vehicle could be chosen.
In the part "Vehicle-specific parameters" the series and I-step should be set. There are two options:
• Fill the fields: Series and I-step.
Format example:
If any of these fields are left empty the following warning will be shown. Despite the warning, the
user can try to establish the connection.
• Read series and I-step from VCM and confirm, or change the values in the following dialog.
64
Information about the established connection are shown on the right hand side in the status bar.
5.2. Choosing a TargetSelector
Each “TargetSelector” is composed of two parts, the “Project” and the “VehicleInfo”. By choosing a
“Project” you determine which imported ODX container data you want to use for the connection.
The “VehicleInfo” defines whether a direct ECU connection or a connection via gateway (e.g. ZGW)
is set up. Thus two TargetSelectors are offered for each imported container, one for direct ECU
connection and one for gateway connection. The dropdown menus “Main series” and “Connection
type” can be used to further filter the list of displayed target selectors.
5.2.1. Connecting via gateway
Gateway connection must be chosen whenever a gateway is installed between the programmer and
the ECU(s) to be programmed. The gateway will route all diagnostic services to the ECU bus system
and back to the tester based on its routing table.

When setting up a gateway connection, a “VehicleInfo” WITHOUT the suffix
“_DIRECT” has to be selected in the connection dialogue.
Valid TargetSelectors for a gateway connection
5.2.2. Direct connection
In the case of a direct connection, the host computer is connected for example via a CANCard or
CANCase or something comparable. That means a direct connection is established to the ECU to be
programmed; no gateway-ECU is used.

When setting up a direct ECU connection a “VehicleInfo” WITH suffix “_DIRECT”
has to be selected.
65
Valid TargetSelectors for a direct ECU connection
5.3. Choosing the physical interface
By selecting the radio buttons in the lower part of the dialogue the user can decide which hardware
interface is used to set up the connection.
5.3.1. Connecting via Ethernet
An Ethernet connection can be set up by either specifying the gateway URL or by selecting a vehicle
by its vehicle identification number (VIN). To set up a vehicle connection the tester and the vehicles’
gateway have to be in the same IP subnet. If there is no DHCP server available in this subnet the
gateway will fall back to a 169.254.x.y local IP address (Windows APIPA addressing). This means an
address in the same subnet (i.e., 169.254.u.v) has to be assigned to the testers’ network interface to
set up the connection, the subnet mask is 255.255.0.0 in this case.
5.3.1.1. Connecting via gateway URL
If one knows the gateways’ IP address a connection can be set up by simply entering the URL.

Specifying the protocol (tcp://) and the port (:6801) is mandatory! Thus
tcp://169.254.47.11:6801 would be a valid gateway URL.
Note that in this example, 6801 corresponds to HSFZ protocol. Other protocols will
use different ports.
Instead of the IP address, the gateways’ host name can also be used in the gateway URL. For a
vehicle with the VIN “00000000000000000” the gateway URL would in this case be
tcp://diagadr10bmwvin00000000000000000.muc:6801.
Connecting via gateway URL
66
5.3.1.2. Connecting via vehicle identification number (VIN)
When opening the connection dialogue and after clicking the “Refresh” button all available vehicles
are detected by a network broadcast and their vehicle identification numbers (VINs) are listed
under “Connection via VIN” in the connection dialogue. A connection to the desired vehicle can be
established by picking it from the drop-down list. If there is no vehicle available “Connection via
VIN” is disabled.
Connecting via VIN
5.3.2. Connecting via ICOM
Basically, there are two ways to set up a connection via ICOM depending on whether the ICOM
forwards messages to the vehicle via D-CAN or via Ethernet. Irrespective of that, the connection to
the ICOM is always set up via TCP/IP.
5.3.2.1. Connecting via ICOM/D-CAN
If the ICOM forwards messages to the vehicle via D-CAN (special ICOM firmware required),
“Connection via ICOM/D-CAN” has to be chosen. The ICOM URL has to be entered in the text field,
the port in this case is 52410 (50000 + 10*0xF1).
Connecting via ICOM/D-CAN
5.3.2.2. Connecting via ICOM/Ethernet
If the ICOM forwards messages to the vehicle via Ethernet, “Connection via ICOM/Ethernet” has to
be chosen. The ICOM URL has to be entered in the text field, the port in this case is 50000 +
10*<gateway diagnostic address>. To forward messages to the ZGW, for example, enter port 50000 +
10*0x10 = 50000 + 10*16 = 50160.
Connecting via ICOM/Ethernet
67
5.3.3. Direct connections
Under the item "Connection via bus" there are two dropdowns. The left dropdown shows the
available buses of the selected series, while the right dropdown lists the available connection
methods.
Below the dropdowns there is an associated input field, which can only be edited if
SYSTEMBUS_ETHERNET and MEDIA_CONVERTER are selected.
Special case connection via bus with Systembus_Ethernet & Media_Converter
The CAN hardware supported by E-Sys as well as the supported driver versions can be found in the
release notes, which are stored under "C:\EC-Apps\E-Sys\lib\environment". Current drivers for the
CAN interfaces are usually available on the manufacturer’s homepage.

Before programming, the connection driver "ProDiaS-CAN-Driver CAN 1" must be
assigned to the CAN channel used for programming via "Control Panel → Vector
Hardware".
Example assignment of "ProDiaS-CAN-Driver CAN 1" to channel 1 of CANcaseXL
68
To connect to an ECU via CAN device, select "Connection via bus" in the connection dialogue. The
drop-down menu on the left specifies the bus name (e.g. FA_CAN), the drop down box on the right
specifies the interface which is VECTOR_DIRECT in this case. Other possible interfaces are
"VECTOR_DIRECT_FLEXRAY" or "MEDIA_CONVERTER".
Connecting directly via FA-CAN
69

When connecting to the D_CAN you must not select a "VehicleInfo" with the suffix
"_DIRECT" since you will communicate with the ECUs via the gateway.
5.4. Choosing vehicle-specific parameters
Series and I-step (shipment) of the connected vehicle can be specified in the connection dialogue or
read from VCM.
In the dropdown for model series and construction stage, only values that have been entered
previously will appear. These values are validated against a predetermined format (model series
must have a minimum of 3 and a maximum of 4 characters from A-Z & 0-9, I-Step must consist of
exactly 4 characters from A-Z & 0-9 + '-' + exactly 2 characters from 0-9 + '-' + exactly 2 characters
from 0-9 + ' - ' + exactly 3 characters from 0-9). Therefore, it is possible to enter "incorrect" values as
they are not further checked by E-Sys.
Vehicle-specific parameters
Setting those parameters causes E-Sys to use special data from the PDX template for a certain
series/I-step if applicable. Such special data is necessary if certain ECU attributes (e.g., bus
connection) must be differentiated within one main series. It is thus recommended to specify or
read those parameters from VCM whenever possible. If the parameters are not set (empty fields), ESys uses default data for the main series, and the following warning will be shown.
Warning displayed when Vehicle-specific parameters are not specified
Despite the warning, the user can try to establish the connection.
5.5. Connection test
To check the connection, it is recommended to read the SVT from the vehicle/ECUs after setting up
the connection. The function "Read (ECU)" is for instance located in module "Comfort Mode → TALCalculating". If the connection has been set up successfully, the configuration of all connected ECUs
will be displayed in the left module pane. If an error occurs or the pane remains empty, please
check for the connection settings again!
Read SVT_actual from ECUs
70
5.6. HTTP server
When a connection is established, an HTTP server is started if the following conditions are met:
• The property HttpUpdate.Activation is set to true (i.e., HttpUpdate.Activation=true)
• The connection type is: gateway URL, ICOM/ETHERNET, ICOM/VCPI, VIN or BUS.
 ICOM/CAN won’t start the server.
By default, this HTTP server is listening on port 8888. However, this port can be changed by
specifying the HttpUpdate.ServerPort property (e.g., HttpUpdate.ServerPort=8080). The valid
HTTP ports values are 8000, 8080, 8888 or any value between 12000 and 13000.
71
Chapter 6. Executing a TAL
In the module TAL-Processing a TAL is processed.
A TAL is an action plan to be processed on a single ECU, a system of ECUs or the entire vehicle. It
doesn’t matter where the TAL is obtained from: it can be loaded from the file system or from
another E-Sys module. A TAL consists at least of one TAL line, and there is a maximum of one TAL
line for every ECU and transaction category.
If you try to execute a TAL with assembly or disassembly of hardware a message pops up, and you
can save the information of the ECU by the menu "Extras→Individual data backup" that is specific
for this individual ECU. Information that can’t be retrieved on the HW network nor from other
ECUs of the same type. These files are saved in a backup directory. Now the HW can be exchanged
and the information added to the TAL in Creating a TAL module. See there further Information.

Before starting the TAL processing, a BAT/HAF verification is carried out. It checks
whether a BAT/HAF control unit is installed. If this is the case, the status of switch
S1 is determined. When the switch is open, a message appears informing the user
about possible risks for the TAL-execution process.
6.1. General procedure
In order to be able to start the process of TAL processing, at least the following steps are necessary:
1. Loading a correct TAL via the "…" button
2. If necessary, specification of token information (see subsequent chapter)
3. Providing a valid VIN (vehicle identification number)
As an alternative to manual entry in a text field, the VIN can also be read from a loaded vehicle
order (FA) or directly from the VCM ("Read VIN (VCM)" button).
The FA itself can also be read from the VCM, if available ("Read FA (VCM)" button).
4. Start of the operation
General controls in the TAL execution module
72
TAL and FA can also be opened via the "Edit" button in the editor provided for this purpose.
Optionally, an SVT can also be specified, which is then written to the VCM as SVT target before the
TAL is processed (provided that the VCM supports SVT version 6 or higher).

If the selected TAL contains coding transactions, a VIN is not sufficient for
processing, a suitable FA (faVersion="3") is required. Vehicle orders can be
processed comfortably with the tool [FA_GEN].
The controls at the bottom of above figure have the following functions:
• Start: The TAL processing is started and E-Sys automatically switches to the monitoring
dashboard (cf. Monitoring Dashboard). If a TAL processing is running, the label changes to
"Pause" and the processing can be interrupted.
• Stop: Cancels the TAL processing. Is only activated when processing is started.
• Check SWE availability: Here, a check of the SWE availability can be triggered manually
before the start of the local loop processing. This is useful if the automatic check has been
deselected in the settings (cf. Options).
• Check programming protection: Before starting a TAL processing, you can check whether
ECUs are affected by Basic/ Plus programming protection. In this case, program protection
tokens are required, see details in the next chapter.
• Details: This button takes you to the "TALSTATUS Viewer" module, where details about the flash
run are displayed.
6.2. Programming Protection
To minimize security risks, for example due to old software versions, programming protection was
introduced in SP25, whereby certain flash operations require authorization. In this case, a Secure
Token is required for execution.
In this case, programming protection refers to individual control units and depends on the mode.
"Basic" programming protection is used for devices in field mode, while "Plus" programming
protection is used for ECUs in plant mode.
73
"Basic" tokens can be determined automatically under certain circumstances. For this purpose, the
client certificate and the URLs for accessing the SFA backend must be set up (see SFA/ECU-Mode
Expert Mode). Without a configured backend, however, or in the case of "Plus" program protection,
the token required in each case must be requested with a token request in the SFA backend or from
the CBB.

• It is possible to generate a token for Program Protection Plus or to use a signed
token, even if the ECU UID could not be read from all ECUs. If at least one ECU
has responded to the request (ECU-UID), the process is continued. To use this
option, TalExecution.param.flashProtectionPlusOptimistic=true must be set in
the Esys.properties file.
• When loading a token file, the content of the file is not checked for validity.
This happens only when a TAL processing is started.
6.2.1. Check for Programming Protection
The type of programming protection that may be necessary can be determined via the button Check
programming protection. If corresponding tokens are necessary, they are displayed in the following
dialog.
74
If no components are affected, only the following information is displayed:
For components with programming protection "Basic" without backend connection and for those
with programming protection "Plus", a manual request for a token is necessary. The procedure for
this is described in the following section.
6.2.1.1. Create manual request
The request file can be created for programming protection "Basic" (ECUs in Field-Mode) or
programming protection "Plus" (ECUs in Plant-Mode) with the button "Create request file".
The file format of the request as well as of a token received later differs in the procedures:
75
• Basic: JSON format
• Plus: XML format
With this request file the user has to manually send it to the respective backend and get the token
file response, to then upload it in E-Sys (see Load Programming Protection Token File).

• The Plant-Mode (PLUS) offline/manually request file creation is working and
creating xml files, however E-Sys is only accepting JSON Signed Token Files.
• Users (with the proper Access roles) are able to manually create the plus token
files using the ASBC Secure Feature Activation App from the B2B portal.
6.2.1.2. Load Programming Protection Token File
As soon as the signed token file is available from the respective backend, it can be loaded via the "…
" button. The file path is displayed in the field next to it. As soon as the token is loaded and if it is
actually needed, it is automatically used during the TAL processing.

When loading a token file, the content of the file is not checked for validity. This
only happens when a TAL processing is started.
6.2.2. Programming Protection module
The Programming Protection module allows the user to read the programming protection status for
a set of selected ECUs.
The ECUs available for selection are determined by an SVT that can be directly accessed through
the connection or imported.
Upon reading the SVT, you have the option to select a single ECU or multiple ECUs simultaneously
from a provided set. If no selection is done, all ECUs displayed at the SVT tree will be considered.
Once the ECU(s) is chosen, you can query the respective programming status by selecting the
corresponding button.
76
GUI Elements
Read / load SVT Generates the current SVT of the entire vehicle.
In the svt-tree view are only the ECUs of the SVT
displayed.
Read / Edit VIN Read the VIN out of the vehicle. Alternative has
the user the option to edit the VIN manually.
Read programming protection status Allows to read the programming protection
status to all selected ECU(s)
Tree View Allows to select the ECU(s).
6.3. Mirror Protocol
Transaction classes of the Mirror Protocol can be used for ECUs with SP2025. As soon as the
transactions to be processed contain such transactions, at least one programming token is usually
also necessary.
The following transaction classes are used for the Mirror Protocol:
• ecuPoll
• ecuActivate
• ecuMirrorDeploy
Depending on the procedure, different tokens are required:
• Processing in plant mode: Required
• Signed token: Unsigned token is used for preparation
77
• SFA Programming Token: Required
• No authentication: Optional
Possibilities of token creation for the Mirror Protocol
 An unsigned Programming Token is required for all authentication methods.
The creation of an unsigned token is done via the button "Create unsigned token". Alternatively, an
already created unsigned token can be loaded ("…" button on the same line). When creating the
token, two files are created, an XML file, as well as a JSON file, which are both needed. When
loading an existing unsigned token, both files must also be present.
6.3.1. Delta SWE flash
The difference between an older and a newer SWE version is called delta SWE. ECUs which
implement the Mirror Protocol must implement a delta mechanism which requires only the
transmission of the binary difference between and old and the new to be installed SWE version.
GenCore and DeltaInstaller are used to respectively calculate and install deltas. Information about
those tools can be found here: Delta overview
Flashing delta SWEs has the same process as Full, but of course, the "Enable Delta SWE flash"
button in "Parameters" tab must be selected and the required SWEs must be present and properly
formatted in the container. TAL execution will fail at preparation phase if one or more deltas are
not found at the PSdZ data folder.
The user is also able to select, for each SWE defined in a given TAL, if full flash or delta flash shall
be processed.
This attribute can be changed in the TAL xml file, by adding a useDeltaSwe attribute flag with a
boolean value ("true","false") at the ecuMirrorDeployTA parameter. This value is true by default
→ if useDeltaSwe is not set it will have the value true.
...
<talLine id="tl_3" status="Executable" baseVariant="CCU2" diagAddress="3A">
  <ecuMirrorDeploy status="Executable">
  <ecuMirrorDeployTA useDeltaSwe="false" status="NotExecutable">
  . . .
  </ecuMirrorDeployTA>
  </ecuMirrorDeploy>
</talLine>
...
78
Or it can be changed on the TAL editor in the GUI:
This works with the Enable Delta SWE flash global choice in the following way:
• If enableDeltaSweFlash = false, then what was chosen at TA level (useDeltaSwe = true or false),
is not considered.
◦ example: If enableDeltaSweFlash = false and useDeltaSwe = true → no delta flash
• If enableDeltaSweFlash = true and useDeltaSwe = false for a specific sgbmid → delta flash will
happen for other able swe except for that specific sgbmid.

This functionality does not work for the parameter
smacEcuMirrorDeployOnMasterTA, only for the ecuMirrorDeployTA.
Delta SWEs, after being imported into PSdZ, have both versions in its names followed by the delta
algorithm: <ProcessClass>_<SGBMID>.bsw<TargetVersion><SourceVersion><PV>
Here is an example:
"swfk_00005a13.bsw.001_020_080-001_018_085-SP21_DEFAULT_C7"
The components of the BSW itself are named as follows:
• xml and .bin file carry the versioning as above
◦ btld_00007d43.bin.004_047_051-004_047_020-SP21_DEFAULT_LARGE_C7
◦ btld_00007d43.xml.004_047_051-004_047_020-SP21_DEFAULT_LARGE_C7
• json, .sig are named same as in full SWE (there are no specific manifest and key for Delta, here
79
always the info from the target state is used
◦ btld_00007d43_004_047_051.json
◦ btld_00007d43_004_047_051.sig
• SWE parts are named as specified in the manifest.
◦ btld_boot.img.bin
Containers with deltas include an additional file: delta_inst.xml (generated by CI systems) and/or
deltamap.xml (generated by tool).
Example for delta_inst.xml:
<?xml version='1.0' encoding='UTF-8' standalone='yes'?>
<DELTAINST>
  <ECU name="DUMMY-ECU">
  <INSTCOMP processClass="swfl" identifier="87654321" version="111_111_111"
paramRef="SP21_DEFAULT_LARGE_C7"/>
  </ECU>
</DELTAINST>
Example for delta_map.xml:
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?>
<DELTAMAP xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
xsi:noNamespaceSchemaLocation="deltamap.xsd">
  <DELTA file="swfl_00007d7f.bsw.001_048_023-001_047_140-SP21_DEFAULT">
  <TO processClass="SWFL" identifier="00007d7f" version="001_048_023" />
  <FROM processClass="SWFL" identifier="00007d7f" version="001_047_140" />
  <INSTALLER processClass="SWFL" identifier="00007d78" version="001_047_140" />
  </DELTA>
</DELTAMAP>
Also as an example, here is a container configured to flash with deltas for a particular SWE:
Container: U006_23_07_505_Q.077_003_024.pdx
• Index contains reference to full SWE:
<ABLOCK UPD="UNDEFINED">
  <SHORT-NAME>swe_swfk_swfk_0000a323_bsw</SHORT-NAME>
  <CATEGORY>BINARY</CATEGORY>
  <FILES>
  <FILE CREATION-DATE="2023-03-22Z" CREATOR="E-Sys" MIME-TYPE="swfk/bsw"
>U006_23_07_505_Q_077_003_024/swe/swfk/swfk_0000a323.bsw.001_056_014</FILE>
  </FILES>
</ABLOCK>
80
As well as delta:
<ABLOCK UPD="UNDEFINED">
  <SHORT-NAME>swfk_0000a323.bsw.001_056_014-001_056_007-
SP21_DEFAULT_LARGE_C8</SHORT-NAME>
  <CATEGORY>BINARY</CATEGORY>
  <FILES>
  <FILE CREATION-DATE="2023-03-24Z" CREATOR="ANONYMOUS" MIME-TYPE="swfk/delta"
>U006_23_07_505_Q_077_003_024/swe/swfk/swfk_0000a323.bsw.001_056_014-001_056_007-
SP21_DEFAULT_LARGE_C8</FILE>
  </FILES>
</ABLOCK>
• U006_23_07_505_Q_077_003_024\config\deltamap.xml contains:
  <DELTA file="swfk_0000a323.bsw.001_056_014-001_056_007-SP21_DEFAULT_LARGE_C8">
  <TO identifier="0000a323" processClass="SWFK" version="001_056_014"/>
  <FROM identifier="0000a323" processClass="SWFK" version="001_056_007"/>
  <INSTALLER identifier="0000abd2" processClass="SWFL" version="001_056_007"/>
  </DELTA>
• The full and delta SWEs are in the appropriate folder:
◦ U006_23_07_505_Q_077_003_024\swe\swfk\swfk_0000a323.bsw.001_056_014
◦ U006_23_07_505_Q_077_003_024\swe\swfk\swfk_0000a323.bsw.001_056_014-001_056_007-
SP21_DEFAULT_LARGE_C8
6.3.2. Signed Token
Because some ECUs do not require the token to be signed, it is possible to use an unsigned token as
a signed token. In these cases, the user does not need to load the signed token – the field for loading
it can be left empty – only the authentication method “Signed Token” needs to be selected.
For these cases, the process of generating the unsigned token can be automated. So, when the
authentication method is “Signed Token” and no file containing the unsigned token has been
provided, an unsigned token will be automatically generated before TAL processing begins. This
automatic process creates the following two files in the default directory for programming tokens
(e.g., C:\Data\ProgrammingTokens):
• ProgrammingToken_YYYYMMDD_HHMMSS.xml
• ProgrammingToken_YYYYMMDD_HHMMSS_UnsignedMirrorProtocolToken.json
Where YYYYMMDD_HHMMSS is the timestamp when the files were created.
It is important to note that if the user provides both unsigned and signed files, the signed files will
be used.
81
6.3.3. SFA token
In addition to the unsigned token, an SFA token with the feature ID for the mirror token is required.
To load an SFA token, the "SFA Programming Token" selection button is activated and the token is
loaded via the "…" button next to it.
6.3.4. Plant Mode
This option is selected via "Processing in plant mode".
In addition to the unsigned token, a plant mode token is required. This can either be loaded
manually ("…" button) or it is automatically loaded by E-Sys from the backend during TAL
processing. The prerequisite for this is a connection to the backend.
6.3.5. No authentication
If no authentication is required, this option can be selected. If an unsigned token is loaded, it is set
during TAL processing, but it is not required.
6.4. Partial programming (ECUs/transaction classes)
In the "ECU" tab, it is possible to exclude certain ECUs or transaction classes from processing before
starting the TAL execution. A matrix can be used to specifically control which transaction
categories of the loaded TAL are to be executed for which ECU. Transaction classes (columns) are
only displayed if a corresponding transaction exists in the TAL for at least one ECU. Transactions
which are not contained in the TAL, but which are displayed due to the matrix structure, cannot be
selected and are displayed grayed out. If the status of a transaction differs from "executable", the
differing status is displayed instead of the selection box.
TAL matrix for targeted selection of transactions

Transactions whose status differs from "executable" are always executed. Errorfree processing of the TAL is then not possible.
82
6.5. Setting options for TAL processing
This tab allows to control the TAL processing features.
The following parameters can be adjusted:
• Parallel programming:
Defines whether the individual transactions in the TAL are to be processed sequentially or in
parallel (default: active).
• Retries on error:
Defines the maximum number of times transactions within the TAL are repeated in the event of
an error (default: 1).
• Check programming counter:
Defines whether the programming counter status of the control units is to be evaluated (default:
active).
Important: The programming counter can only be ignored with tester insert identifier "F"
(development).
• Disable HTTP transfer:
Specifies whether to disable the PSdZ internal HTTP server for flashing over Ethernet (default:
inactive).
83
• Automatically fill InstalledECUList of the TAL before processing:
Defines whether the InstalledEcuList of the TAL used by E-Sys is to be adapted to the actual
status read out before the TAL is processed. In this case, the existing list can either be
supplemented or overwritten (default: active + supplement).
• Mileage for fingerprint:
Allows to define a mileage for the flash fingerprint. (Default: 0)
• Disable Response on Event (RoE) during TAL processing: Defines whether a diagnostic
command to deactivate the RoEs is sent to all ECUs at the start of the TAL processing.

To ensure an error-free flash run with a direct flash, this function must be
deactivated (=not set!). When flashing via a gateway, this function can be selected.
(Recommendation: = not set)
• Perform optimized bootloader flash:
Specifies whether the TAL is processed in an optimized manner after a bootloader update.
Currently, during TAL generation for an ECU after a bootloader update, all software units are
instructed to be programmed, regardless of whether they are still present on the ECU or not.
This potentially results in unnecessary loss of time as software units that are already present on
the ECU are programmed again. To avoid unnecessary programming, this switch can be
activated. It should be noted that the optimized bootloader flash can only be performed on ECUs
that support this functionality. (Default: inactive)
• Use locally available NCD files:
Specifies whether a directory with pre-signed NCD files should be used instead of performing
the calculation and signing during TAL processing.
No check is made to see if all required NCD files are present or signed. All missing NCD records
are calculated and signed during TAL processing if this is possible. In the process, the contents
of the specified directory are neither overwritten nor completed. (Default: inactive)
• Enable delta SWE flash The difference between an older and a newer SWE version is called
delta SWE. ECUs which implement the Mirror Protocol must implement a delta mechanism
which requires only the transmission of the binary difference between and old and the new to
be installed SWE version.
This specifies if only this difference will be flashed. For now, we consider only the basic scenario
where the user can globally select full or delta flashing. In every case, unless there is specific
indication of otherwise, the default mode is full.
• Activate programming mode for switchable control units
Determines whether switchable ECUs are switched to programming mode during TAL
processing. If ECUs are not switched over, this may lead to reduced parallelism and reduced
block sizes during programming and thus longer programming times. In addition, the table can
be used to specify exactly which ECUs will be switched. Since it is not known which ECUs act as
gateway before the flash, all ECUs from the TAL are listed here. Accordingly, the user must know
which ECUs can actually be switched.
If an ECU isn’t listed in the blacklist nor in the whitelist, PSdZ decides by internal calculation
strategies whether the ECU is switched or not (as a rule of thumb, switchable ECUs are always
switched).
84
The columns of the table have the following functions:
1. ID base: Identification of the ECU by means of the name of the base variant with appended
diagnostic address (hexadecimal).
2. Blacklist: ECU is not switched
3. Whitelist: ECU is switched if it is switchable

If an ECU is blacklisted, it is advisable to whitelist all other ECUs. It should also be
noted that ECUs can only be switched if central gateways are not included in the
blacklist.
• UDS fallback
If an HTTP flash is to be performed for an ECU, a check of the HTTP connection is currently
initiated on the ECU before the start of the data transfer. If this is negative, programming via the
UDS protocol is started as a 'fallback' solution.
The 'UDS fallback' table can be used to specify exactly which ECUs are allowed to access the UDS
flash in the event of an error and which are not. If the fallback mechanism is to be deactivated
for an ECU and an error occurs in the HTTP transmission, the flash process for this ECU is
aborted with an error. Since it is not known before the flash which control units support an
HTTP flash, all control units from the TAL are shown here. The columns of the table have the
following functions:
1. ID base: Identification of the ECU by means of the name of the base variant with appended
diagnostic address (hexadecimal).
2. Prevent UDS fallback: ECU does not fall back to the UDS flash in case of faulty HTTP flash.
• Programming Protection Status Check
Determines a set of ECUs that should execute the read status programming protection during
TAL Processing. When this option is used, the result is not evaluated for the TAL execution
status, however PSdZ logs it, allowing later analysis in case of errors.
1. ID base: Identification of the ECU by means of the name of the base variant with appended
diagnostic address (hexadecimal).
85
2. Programming Protection Status: ECU will execute the read status programming protection
during TAL Processing.
• SMAC: Force SWEs transmission:
Specifies whether all software units (SWEs) for SMAC should always be transmitted. If disabled,
only required units are transmitted. Software units that are already present and valid on the
Smart Actuator are skipped.
• Disable TAS:
Defines whether the functionality of the Tester Assistant (TAS) should be disabled during TAL
processing.
6.6. Monitoring Dashboard
Element Description
Progress Bar Visualization of process progress.
Select Events button Specifies which log events should be added to the Status panel. A
pop-up window appears in which the user selects type of events.
Log Events checkbox If selected, logs the events of the selected types.
Save button Saves the status panel content to a file. A pop-up window appears in
which the user specifies the file in which to save the information.
Clear button Clears the Monitoring Dashboard.
Status panel Display text information related to the process execution.
86
Chapter 7. Coding
Coding can be used to set programmable functions of ECUs. The Coding expert module provides the
user with a way of coding individual ECUs without having to use a transaction list (cf Executing a
TAL).
7.1. Preparation
To prepare for coding, a vehicle connection must first be established (see Connecting). As soon as it
is established, a vehicle order (FA) can be read out and saved via the connection. Alternatively, an
existing FA can be loaded via the file system. The "Edit" button switches to the FA editor (see FA/FP
Edit).
Once a FA is open, it can be activated via the context menu (usually automatically).
Activate FA (vehicle order)
After activating the vehicle order, the vehicle profile is determined and displayed in the right area.
The area cannot be changed, the vehicle profile can be saved as an XML file via the context menu.
Vehicle profile
In the next step, an SVT (system variant table) is read or loaded. The "Read (VCM)" or "Read (ECU)"
buttons are available for reading from the vehicle using VCM or ECU. After loading, the SVT can be
stored in the file system via "Save" for later use. Alternatively, an existing SVT can be loaded from
87
the file system. The "Edit" button changes to the SVT editor (see Create and edit SVTs).
Prepare SVT
As soon as an SVT is available, it is displayed in the "System Variant Table (SVT)" area. The actual
state of the installed devices is always displayed in blue.
7.2. Read coding data
The current coding of one or more ECUs can be read out via the "Read coding data" context menu or
via the button of the same name in the "Coding" area. The result is displayed in a dialog.
Normally, the coding verification stamp (CPS) is verified, the NCD (net coding data) is read and
saved under the data directory in the CAF folder.
Read coding data
After the successful reading of the coding data, the marked CAFD entry turns into an expandable
node. Below is the read-out NCD, which is also stored as a file in the CAF folder in the data
directory.
Display read NCD
88
The read-out NCDs can be edited directly. To do this, you can switch directly to the FDL editor via
the context menu (for a description, see Edit function data lists (FDL)).
Edit NCD
7.3. Perform coding
In order to be able to carry out the coding, suitable NCD data must be available in the CAF folder for
the selected control unit(s). To start, either the context menu "Coding" or the button with the same
name can be used. The coding uses the technique of TAL processing, accordingly the process can
also be accelerated here via the checkbox "Parallel TAL execution" via parallel processing.
Coding area
During the coding process, a monitoring dashboard is used to show the progress and relevant
messages.
Coding in progress
After the coding process has been completed, a results dialog appears in which the respective
coding status is displayed.
89
Completion of the coding
7.4. Additional functions
7.4.1. Code delivery state
The control units can be reset to the initial coding state via the "Coding delivery state" button.
7.4.2. Read CPS
The button of the same name leads to a dialog in which the reading result for the coding
verification stamp (CPS) is displayed. The code check stamp is used by the respective control unit
for validation purposes.
Read coding check stamp
7.4.3. NCD code
When NCDs are processed (see Read coding data), they can be coded directly into the selected ECUs
using the "Code NCD" button.
NCD Coding
90
7.4.4. SVT filter and reset
To make the SVT tree clearer, a restriction to certain software units can be made. The others will
then no longer be displayed until "All" is selected again.
SVT filter/reset
To unload a loaded SVT actual or SVT target and thus reset the tree, the "SVT Reset" button is used.
7.5. Compare and determine CAFs
7.5.1. Comparison SVT-actual/SVT-target
It is possible to compare version changes of the CAFs by loading a SVT target in addition to the SVT
actual. For this purpose, the SVT Target area is available on the right side, which functionally
corresponds to the same area in the TAL processing.
Once both SVTs are loaded, the differences are highlighted in color in the SVT.
CAF comparison with SVT actual/target
7.5.2. Detect CAF for SWE
As soon as an ECU or a software unit is marked, the "Detect CAF for SWE" button is active. It can be
used to directly determine and display the matching CAF for a software unit.
Detect CAF for SWE

7.6. Batch
