authentication, etc.).
92
Chapter 8. Special features for L4-ECUs
8.1. Mapping
To be able to treat KWP2000-ECUs adopted from a prior series, logistic information from those ECUs
(assembly number, hardware number, hardware reference …) has to be mapped to SGBM
identifiers. This is achieved by means of XML mapping files which are generated in the
“Eintrittskarteneditor (EKE)” and added to the PDX container beneath the “Config” element:
Container with mapping files for AMP_TOP and MULF_Basis
The following list briefly describes the existing mapping files and the mapping flow:
• BTLD: Maps the ECU hardware reference to the SGBM-ID and the version of the bootloader
(BTLD).
• CAFD: Maps the assembly number to the SGBM-ID of the CAF file (CAFD). The CAF main version
is derived from the parameter BMW_vehicleManufacturerCodingIndex which is part of the ECU
response to the diagnostic service "Ident_Lesen". Subversion and patch version are derived
from the diagnostic service "Aenderungsindex der Codierdaten lesen".
• HWEL: Maps physical ECU hardware number (PECUHN) and hardware reference (ZZZPPP) to
the SGBM-ID and the version of the hardware module (HWEL). If the hardware number cannot
be read HWEL-mapping is based on the hardware reference only.
• TYPNR: Maps the assembly number to the type approval number ("Typprüfnummer").
• ZB: Maps the assembly number and the program reference (respectively the data reference) to
the application (and data) software units (SGBM-IDs and versions). If ECU information and
mapping files differ in the program version only the SGBM-IDs are mapped and versions are set
to 000_000_000.
93
8.2. AIFContents
When programming a KWP2000-ECU in E-Sys the content of the user info field (AIFContents) has to
be filled in the TAL:
TAL with AIContents for MULF_Basis
The following elements have to be filled (if they have not been generated automatically):
• BmwAssemblyNumber: Assembly number written to AIF/UIF after programming
• BmwCalibrationDataSetNumber: SW number from the _TYPNR mapping file for ECUs with
large AIF (51 or 64 byte), "0000000" otherwise
• BmwExhaustRegulationOrTypeApprovalNumber: Type approval number
(“Typprüfnummer”) from _TYPNR mapping file for exhaust relevant parts, "0000000" otherwise
• PrgRef: Program reference of the software to be programmed

The AIFContents entered in the TAL are written to the ECU after a successful
programming process. Therefore, mapping might not be possible afterwards if this
information is not correct. In this case the ECU would no longer be programmable
with E-Sys.
94
Chapter 9. Recovering individual data
The purpose of recovering individual data (IDR) is to read user specific data from an ECU before
certain ECU actions (exchange, programming …) are performed and to write the data back after
those actions.
IDRlight is a simple variant of IDR used by certain ECUs.
9.1. IDBackup
IDBackup denotes the process of reading and saving individual data. To perform an IDBackup first
an adequate TAL is required. This TAL can be either calculated automatically from an appropriate
SVT-Actual /SVT-Target or can be created manually in the TAL-Editor.
9.1.1. Automatic TAL calculation
To be able to calculate a TAL for IDBackup automatically with E-Sys, a SVT-Actual and a SVT-Target
fulfilling the following qualifications are needed:
• For the IDR-ECU at least, one hardware element (HWEL) had to be different between SVT-Actual
and SVT-Target in either the SGBM-ID or the version. Now it is possible to read out the
individual data memory objects from the ECU.
SVT-Actual and SVT-Target with different HWEL
• If there is no KIS database available to derive an appropriate SVT-Target , it is recommended to
adapt the SVT-Actual in the SVT-Editor (change HWEL) and save it as a SVT-Target. With those
95
two files available a TAL for IDBackup can be calculated in the module "Comfort Mode → TALCalculating".

Warnings might occur during TAL calculation e.g. if KIS is not available. Those
warnings normally do not affect IDBackup and can thus be ignored in this context.
The "ID Backup" button is used for this purpose and starts the IDR TAL calculation. Subsequently,
the TAL can be renamed and saved via the "Save" button. Afterwards, it can be opened in the
"Editors & Viewers → TAL Editor" module or in any XML editor.
ID-Backup TAL
9.1.2. Manual creation
The TAL for IDBackup can also be manually created in the TAL-Editor. At least the following
elements must be added to the TAL:
• A HWInstall transaction for the affected ECU (any content)
• A HWDeinstall transaction for the affected ECU (any content)
• An IDBackup transaction for the affected ECU
For each of these transactions a single TAL-Line must be created. Within the IDBackup transaction
an IDBackupTA or an IDBackupLight element must be created. The default value is IDBackupTA.

Within an IDBackup transaction either an IDBackupTA or an IDBackupLight
element can be added. Thus, the automatically created IDBackupTA element has to
be deleted before an IDBackupLight element can be created.
TAL with IDR transactions in the TAL-Editor
96
9.1.3. Reading and saving individual data
In order to read the individual data, the TAL created in the former steps has to be loaded and
executed in the module "Expert Mode → TAL-Execution". If IDR is successful the TAL executes with
status „FinishedForHWTransactions” and a dialog is automatically opened, asking the user where
to save the individual data. The data is then saved to the XML file IDBackup.bak (possibly additional
files are generated as well) in the specified directory.
Backup files after IDR classic (left), IDR light (middle) and IDR with PIA Client (right)
97
9.2. IDRestore
IDRestore denotes the process of writing individual data back to the ECU. Just like IDBackup the
IDRestore process is triggered by executing a TAL, either calculated automatically or created
manually. Automatic creation only works when the individual data is stored in an IDBackup.bak file
created in the IDBackup process described in the previous section.
9.2.1. Automatic TAL calculation
To calculate the IDRestore transaction in the "Comfort mode → TAL calculation" module, SVT-Actual
and SVT-Target do not have to differ. It is recommended to assign the current SVT-Actual to both
fields so that a correct InstalledECUList is generated. So that an IDRestore transaction is calculated,
the directory with the IDBackup.bak file must be specified in the adjacent field. The IDR TAL
calculation can then be triggered using the "ID Restore" button and the TAL can be saved, which
then contains exactly the data that was stored in the IDBackup.bak file. The TAL generated in this
way thus contains only IDR actions flashing or even coding of ECUs is not possible with this TAL.

Warnings might occur during TAL calculation e.g. if KIS is not available. Those
warnings normally do not affect IDBackup and can thus be neglected in this
context.
TAL calculation settings for IDRestore
9.2.2. Manual creation
Similar to IDBackup the IDRestore TAL can also be created manually. For this purpose, a TAL with a
single TAL-Line containing an IDRestore transaction has to be created in the TAL-Editor (don’t
forget to fill base variant and diagnostic address). Different settings have to be performed
depending on the IDR mode.
1. IDR light:
In order to accomplish an ID restore light, one has to add an IDRestoreLight element to the
IDRestore-TAL-line (this requires to first delete the automatically generated IDRestore element).
Then for each DataRecord a matching Element containing the DataIdentifier and the respective
value (cf. IDBackup.bak) has to be appended. This is done by right-clicking on "IDRestoreLight ᾆ
new ᾆ DataRecord".
TAL for IDRestore (IDR light)
98
2. IDR classic and IDR with PIA client
In order to accomplish an IDRestore for IDR classic or IDR with a PIA client, one has to add an
IDRestore Element to the IDRestore TAL line for each additional file that contains individual
data. Within the IDRestore elements one has to define the MemoryObjectIdentifier, the
MemorySize and the path to the individual data file.
TAL for IDRestore (IDR classic & PIA client)
99
9.2.3. Restore individual data
To finally write back the data to the ECU the calculated or manually created TAL has to be executed
in the module “TAL-Execution”. If the individual data could be restored successfully the TAL
execution will end with the status “Finished”.
100
Chapter 10. OBD-CVN
In the OBD-CVN module, which is in expert mode, CVNs (Calibration Verification Number) can be
read out from the ECUs and calculated from the sub-CVNs of the individual OBD-relevant SWEs.
The calculated and read-out values can be contrasted and compared with each other.
The ECUs and software units required for the calculation of the CVNs are read from an SVT
document. The SVT document can be read from the ECU, from the VCM or from a specified file.
The CVN values and comparison results are written to a report file as text or in XML format.
10.1. GUI
The SVTs recorded in red letters indicate the reference system state of an ECU. The blue ones
indicate the actual state of the ECU. Green entries indicate SVTs with identical reference and actual
state.

Chapter 11. VCM
The VCM module provides functions of the VCM (Vehicle Configuration Management). The VCM is a
component in the vehicle that stores certain states and information of the vehicle. VCM functions
are addressed via a special (trimmed down) vehicle info spec, so that at the start of a session,
communication is first established with the VCM before individual ECUs are addressed.
Two individual ECUs are installed in the vehicle for the VCM. The VCM Master and the VCM Backup.
This ensures almost complete fail-safety, since even if one of the two ECUs is defective, all data is
still saved on the other.
The configuration data can be written by the user directly to the master only. The data can only be
uploaded to the backup control unit as a backup of the master control unit.
VCM module
The module is divided into two areas. In the upper area, there are viewers for the vehicle order, the
vehicle profile, the SVT and the VIN. There is also an editor for the I-steps.
In the lower area, the user is offered the four sub-modules File, Master, Backup and VCM InfoVCMInfo & Status.
11.1. File
VCM File tab
104
In the "File" submodule, actions can be carried out for the files Vehicle Order, Vehicle Profile, SVT
Actual and SVT Target.
The respective files (FA, FP, SVT) can be loaded from the file system via the three-dot button. These
are then displayed graphically in their viewer in the upper area.
With the button "Save as…" the respective files can be stored in the file system and renamed.
The "Edit" button opens the respective editor for FA and SVT and loads the current data into this
editor to make them available for editing.
Element Description
Three-dot button Load respective data (FA, FP or SVT) from filesystem.
Save as Save respective data (FA, FP or SVT) into file system.
Edit Open the respective editor and load current data (FA or SVT) to
provide it for display.

Chapter 12. KDS
In addition to protecting the entire vehicle against theft, it is also important to protect selected
components against theft.
In addition to mechanical measures, an electronic theft protection system called Component Theft
Protection (KDS) has been introduced. This is based on an unbreakable link between the vehicle
and the respective component. When a component is replaced, the control units protected in this
way recognise that they have been installed in another vehicle. Depending on the component, the
functionality is restricted or switched off in this case.
However, for certain applications, such as the replacement of the BCP control unit that houses the
KDS master or the installation of a new (possibly also used) protected component, it must be
possible, regardless of the "faulty" installation of one or more KDS clients that is detected by the
KDS system, for example, to perform a new link between the KDS master and the KDS clients
present in the vehicle. This process is called refurbish.
 Each Refurbish process must be authorised by BMW.
A secure token needs to be used in order to perform the Refurbish process.
This process is carried out in the following steps:
When the fault memory is read out, it is determined whether a control unit has been crossreplaced. If so, a diagnostic job determines which pairing must be renewed. In case of deviations, a
new pairing is necessary for the affected control units. A Secure Token must be requested for this.
12.1. KDS Extended
KDS (anti-theft protection 2.0 and 2.5) based on the secure token sets (see SFA/ECU-Mode Expert
Mode)

The functionalities provided in this module which include direct server access
require to have several preconditions to be fulfilled:
• The system which runs E-Sys must be in a BMW network segment in which the
backend systems (SFA-Backend) are available.
• There must be a valid E-Sys client Certificate imported into E-Sys.
• At least one URL of a valid backend system (SFA-Backend) must be configured
in E-Sys.
A more detailed set of instructions can be found here: HOWTO (only available
within BMW network) - if the link does not automatically open, please validate your
Access Permissions to the shared folder and contact your BMW Contact Person.
108
12.1.1. KDS status
The button Quick check (marked green) starts with a KDS system check. The result is visualized in
the GUI and has one of the following values:
KDS quick check results
MASTER_OK_CLIENT_OK
MASTER_OK_CLIENT_INVALID
MASTER_INVALID_CLIENT_OK
MASTER_INVALID_CLIENT_INVALID
ERROR_CLIENT_NOT_PAIRED
12.1.2. Standard actions
109
These tab can visualize the KDS system. It is separated in the KDS-master and KDS-clients. All KDS
system members are by the KDS-ID.
• Read KDS (marked red): Read the entire KDS system.
• Refurbish process (marked green): [Only with BMW-Intranet connection possible] Identifies
all participants in the KDS system, that have not been correctly paired and is pairing the entire
KDS system.
• Switching operation mode: Change the operation mode for the chose ECUs. If no ECU is selected
the entire KDS system is going to switch. The switch into the modes AUDIT and OPEN requires a
BMW-Intranet connection and the valid client-backend-Certificate (See Authentication settings).
12.1.3. Extended actions
110
Marked blue: Generates a token request file for the chosen ECUs or the entire KDS-system. The
request type can be defined by the drop-down menu, behind the name of the feature ID displayed.

12.2. KDS Comfort mode
KDS Component Theft Protection (or anti-theft protection) is based on the secure token sets (see SFA
and Secure ECU Modes chapter).
The functionalities provided in this module (which include direct server access) require to have
several preconditions to be fulfilled:
• The system which runs E-Sys must be in a BMW network segment in which the backend

• There must be a valid E-Sys client Certificate imported into E-Sys.

A more detailed set of instructions can be found here: HOWTO (only available within BMW

• This module supports only the processing of the entire vehicle.

expert-mode (KDS - Extended)
On the most recent E-sys versions, the Kds Comfort Module handles the Reading of the KDS status
and their Re-pair features for both ServicePack 2021 (BCP-21) - KDS2.0 and EESystem2025 (IP-Basis)

12.2.2. KDS Re-Pair
This button is the “all in one” solution for any user which encounters various issues with KDS in
any vehicle.
In most regular cases, such issues are caused by simply exchanging ECUs between vehicles or by
having the need to exchange ECUs that may have defects.
In such cases the solution is to perform a KDS re-pairing, which involves Secure Tokens that are
authenticating a new KDS Pairing to be performed.
When any “NOT OKAY” results appear after reading the KDS Status, the next step must be to try to
fix those by pressing this “KDS re-pair” button.
Upon pressing the button, E-Sys performs the refurbish process and identifies all participants in the
KDS system, that have not been correctly paired and pairs the entire KDS system.
After the Re-Pairing Process, the KDS Status are again read and the table is updated.

Chapter 13. FAT / AMTS test data generation

Signing of net coding data for ECUs from SP2021 using productive keys requires
the user to login at BMW secure backend. See Login to SWL Security System.
13.1. Loading FA file
The selection of a FA list file must be done in the upper left area of the module. In addition to
loading the FA file, an already loaded FA list can also be edited if required. To do this, the button
"Edit" must be pressed and the loaded FA is opened in the module "FA-Editor".
Loading of a FA-list file
Above figure shows an example of a loaded FA List file. On the left, the content of the file itself is
shown. Here you can also see how many individual vehicle orders (FA) are contained in the file. If
the file contains only one FA, it is automatically activated, a vehicle profile (FP) is generated from it
and displayed as a tree. In addition, all VINs contained in the FAs are made known to the user.

In order to perform NCD test data generation, it must be ensured that the loaded
FA list file matches the selected CAFs. Otherwise, test data set generation will be
aborted with an error message.
Error – NCD test data generation – CAF does not support main series
13.2. Selecting CAFs
Selecting CAFs
115
To generate test data, one or more CAFs must be selected.
The tables in the lower area of the module can be used to define for which CAFs NCD test data sets
are to be calculated. In the left table all available CAFs from the current psdzdata directory are
listed. Single or multiple CAFs can be selected and added to the right table using the button "Add >"
in the middle area. Alternatively, it is possible to add single CAFs to the right table by doubleclicking on them or to add all available CAFs by using the button "Add All >>". Analogous
functionality for adding from the right table to the left one is also available: buttons "< Remove"
and "<< Remove All".
For each CAF in the right pane, a suitable bootloader must be selected. This can be done in several
ways:
• Using the dropdown menu in the column "Bootloader" or by a direct typing. In doing so, the
number of still suitable BTLD IDs is reduced with each character entered.
• Alternatively, the respective base variant can be selected first in the column "Base variant". This
reduced the bootloader list to the BTLD-IDs matching the base variant. This makes the BTLD-ID
selection much easier.
For each calculation process, it is required that all selected CAFs belong to one ECU. For this reason,
all selected CAFs must be assigned to a matching and identical BTLD ID. If this rule is disregarded,
the following error message will show:
Error – NCD test data generation – BTLD-ID selection
116
For the same reason, all CAFs (if more than one is selected) must belong to the same coding version.
It is not possible for an ECU to support multiple coding versions. The user will be informed about
the wrong selection with the following error message:
Error – NCD test data generation – CAF selection

In order to perform NCD test data generation, it must be ensured that the loaded
FA list file matches the selected CAFs. Otherwise, test data set generation will be
aborted with an error message.
13.3. Creation of NCD test data for Coding 1
No test data preparation is required for Coding 1 CAF, since Coding 1 NCDs for coding tests can be
generated and signed independently in the respective tools.
117
If an attempt is made to create NCD test data for a Coding 1 CAF, an error message will be shown to
the user.
13.4. Creation of NCD test data for Coding 2
13.4.1. Preconditions
The calculation of test data for coding 2 requires that exactly one FA has been selected. It is possible
that the loaded FA list file contains several vehicle orders. The selection in the FA tree structure is
decisive.
In the selected FA, the VIN must not match the FAT VIN. The FAT VIN is defined in the
Esys.properties under the key fat.vin. The default value is WBA0000150TSVPG3Z. If the VIN from the FA
matches the FAT VIN, the following message will be shown:
NCD test data for Coding 2 – Precondition
13.4.2. Generation
As soon as a valid FA list file has been loaded and at least one CAF with associated BTLD ID has
been selected, the button "Generate Testsuite data" is activated. By pressing the button, the
generation process of NCD test data can be started.
Button "Generate Testsuite data"
The following NCD test data are generated for Coding 2:
• NCD by calculation method "FA". Signed using VIN from FA
• NCD by calculation method "shipment". Signed using VIN from FA
• NCD by calculation method "FA". Signed using FAT-VIN
• If the CAF contains safety-related functions, the additional NCD data are generated and signed
using VIN from FA. For each safety-related function an extra NCD with a changed coding value
(+1 or -1) is created and stored in the directory according to the function name.
Name of directory: <FA-VIN>_<Function_name_1>
Example: WBA1234000H012345_CountryType_ASIL
118
All created test data are stored in a ZIP archive. The ZIP file is placed beneath following path:
<NCD-Directory>\Testdaten\<BTLD_ID>_FatTestData_<yyyyMMdd_HHmmss>.zip
The content of ZIP file:
• FA: contains using FA List file
• <FA-VIN>: contains NCDs signed using FA-VIN
• <FA-VIN>_DEF: contains Default NCDs signed using FA-VIN
• <FAT-VIN>: contains NCDs signed using FAT-VIN
additional CAFs with modified coding values in safety-relevant functions:
• <FA-VIN>_<Function_name_1> contains NCD signed using FA-VIN
• <FA-VIN>_<Function_name_2> contains NCD signed using FA-VIN
• <FA-VIN>_<Function_name_3> contains NCD signed using FA-VIN
• <FA-VIN>_<Function_name_4> contains NCD signed using FA-VIN
• …
Example of successfully generated NCD test data for Coding 2:
Result – NCD Test data for Coding 2
At the end of the generation a report dialog appears to inform the user about the process. In
addition to the general calculation information, all errors that may have occurred are also logged in
the report. If required, the contents of the report dialog can be saved to a file using the "Save"
button.
Report – NCD Test data for Coding 2
119
13.5. Creation of NCD test data for Coding 3
13.5.1. Preconditions
For the calculation of test data for Coding 3, an FA list file must be loaded with exactly 2 FAs, that
must not be identical. This is necessary to get 2 different VPC values for negative tests. In this case,
the selection in the FA tree structure is also irrelevant. Only the content of the file is decisive.
If the FA list file contains only one FA or more than two FAs, the user is informed accordingly.
In addition to the number of FAs, several other criteria regarding the content of the FA list file must
also be considered:
• VINs in both FAs must be different
• VINs in the FAs must be test VINs (11th character of the long VIN is "H").
• Additionally, both FAs must differ in at least one of the following ways:
◦ Colour Code (colourCode)
◦ Fabric Code (fabricCode)
◦ Time Criteria (timeCriteria)
◦ SA entries (saCodes)
◦ E entries (eCodes)
◦ K entries (hoCodes)
If any of the above preconditions is not met, the calculation process will be aborted with the
following error message:
NCD test data for Coding 3 – Precondition
120
13.5.2. Generation

activated when a valid FA list file has been loaded and at least one CAF with the corresponding

started.
The following NCD test data are generated for Coding 3:

◦ Calculated using FA1
◦ Signed using VIN from FA1
• NCD B:

◦ Signed using VIN from FA2
• NCD C:
◦ Calculated using FA2, containing VIN from FA1
◦ Signed using VIN from FA1
• NCD D:
◦ Calculated using FA2
◦ Signed using VIN from FA2
• NCD DEFAULT:
◦ NCD by calculation method "shipment".
◦ Signed using VIN from FA
◦ Signed using Default Long-VIN comprising FF in Hex (String "ÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿÿ")
• If the CAF contains safety-related functions, the additional NCD data are generated and signed
using VIN from FA. For each safety-related function an extra NCD with a changed coding value
(+1 or -1) is created and saved in the directory according to the function name.
Name of directory: ASIL\<Function_name_1>
Example: ASIL\CountryType_ASIL
121
All created test data are stored in a ZIP archive. The ZIP file is placed beneath following path:
<NCD-Directory>\Testdaten\<BTLD_ID>_AmTSTestData_<yyyyMMdd_HHmmss>.zip

Chapter 14. SFA and secure ECU-mode
Secure Feature Activation (SFA) and ECU-Mode are system functions that have been developed and
introduced for ECUs with SP2021.
SFA is a system function for SP2021. This enables certain ECU functions (features) to be
subsequently controlled (activated / deactivated). However, it is a prerequisite that the
corresponding ECUs are SFA-capable.
SFA is the successor technology to Sweeping Technologies (SWT) / activation codes (FSCs).
Activations / deactivations are carried out by importing individual secure tokens, which must be
obtained either through direct use of the BMW backend system or, if the E-Sys client is outside the
BMW network, through the B2B web application.
Secure ECU Modes is a system function for SP2021 that makes it possible to bring ECUs into
different defined states with the aim of protecting the ECU functions that are only necessary for
development purposes or vehicle commissioning. I.e. not to make these available in customer
operations.
There is a total of three modes in which an ECU can be set:
1. Field - Vehicle at customers
2. Plant - Vehicle in production
3. Engineering - Vehicle in development.
A special secure token is also required to switch to the respective ECU mode (except "Field"), which
can be queried directly from the BMW backend system or indirectly via the B2B portal, as with SFA.
Before starting any SFA or Secure ECU-Mode functionalities, an SVT-Actual (SVT-Ist) must first be
loaded or read from the vehicle:
Load SVT-Actual
E-Sys then creates an SVT tree view in the right-hand GUI area in which all ECUs that support SFA
are displayed. The information is also displayed on each ECU node: Basic variant, hexadecimal ECU
address in square brackets, ECU UID in brackets and active ECU mode.
Example: 
The second necessary step is to read the VIN from the vehicle or, if SVT-Actual was loaded as a file,
to enter it manually in the VIN input field.
124
E-Sys offers the user a comfort and an expert mode for Secure ECU Modes and SFA.
14.1. SFA/ECU-Mode Comfort Mode
To call up the SFA and ECU mode modules in comfort mode, press the "SFA" button on the left edge
of the E-Sys:
Module SFA / ECU Mode
A GUI interface is then displayed which only offers two tabs: "Online" and "Offline".

In the comfort mode, the functionalities are simplified and offered in a reduced
extent.
ECU mode switchover or the SFA features manipulations are only possible on all
ECUs listed in the SVT tree view. I.e., a selection of one or more nodes in the SVT
tree view is not possible in comfort mode.
This is what is known as the “Whole Vehicle Treatment”.
14.1.1. SFA/ECU-Mode online
Module SFA / ECU Mode Online
ECU-Mode:
125
In order to determine the currently active ECU mode for each ECU and to display it in the SVT tree
view, the user must press the "Read ECU-mode" button. Communication is started with every ECU
that supports SFA and its actual ECU mode is queried. The SVT tree structure is then updated in ESys.
 The Online Mode requires the E-Sys client to be on the BMW intranet.
All SFA-capable ECUs can be switched to the respective mode by simply pressing the "Engineering
Mode" or "Plant Mode" buttons.
Communication with the BMW backend is completely transparent for the user, all necessary secure
tokens are obtained and imported into the ECUs. All information is then updated in the SVT tree
view in E-Sys.
The switching of ECUs to the field mode is done by pressing the button "Field Mode" and regardless
of whether the E-Sys is currently connected to the network or not, as this process does not require a
secure token.
SFA:
In order to determine the status of all features (activated, deactivated, etc.) for each control device
shown in the SVT tree view, the user must press the "Read actual SFA state" button. Communication
with every SFA-capable ECU is started and its features are queried. The SVT tree structure is then
updated in E-Sys so that each ECU node can be opened and all existing features can be displayed.
Example of an SVT Tree Structure
By pressing the "Write SFA package for order" button, the features in all ECUs can be restored to
the original status that was defined in the factory for SFA-capable ECUs.
Communication with the BMW backend is completely transparent for the user, all necessary secure
tokens are obtained and imported into the ECUs. The relevant information is then updated in the
SVT tree view in E-Sys.
126
 This process requires the E-Sys client to be on the BMW intranet.
The functionality "incl. DELETE Token" means that all active features that are no longer available
according to the target status are to be deleted (deactivated). If this is done, a new secure token
must be generated and imported if the feature is to be activated again at a later point in time.
14.1.2. SFA/ECU-Mode offline
Module SFA / ECU-Mode Offline
 All functions in this tab can also be carried without BMW intranet connection.
ECU-Mode:
• The button “Read Ecu-Mode”
◦ In order to determine the currently active ECU mode for all ECU’s and to display it in the SVT
tree view, the user must press the "Read ECU-Mode" button. Communication is started with
the affected ECUs and their actual ECU modes are queried. The relevant information is then
updated in the SVT tree structure in E-Sys.
• The buttons "Create request file Engineering Mode" or "Create request file Plant Mode"
◦ Must be activated each time the user wants to generate a request (in the form of a JSON file)
for the procurement of secure tokens, which can then be sent manually via B2B web
application to the BMW backend system and thus trigger the calculation of secure tokens for
all ECUs. The created request files are saved locally in a subfolder in the E-Sys data folder
"SFA".
• The button “Field Mode”
127
◦ Switches all ECUs in the SVT tree view to field mode. As in Comfort Mode, no secure tokens
are required for this.
• The input field "File Name"
◦ Response files downloaded via the B2B web application, which were returned by the BMW
backend system and which contain all the required secure tokens, can be saved locally for
later use.
◦ These can then be loaded into E-Sys → "File Name:" input field.
• The Dropdown "Mode"
◦ The dropdown shows one of the following values: "Plant Mode", "Engineering Mode", "Field
Mode", "Mixed" or "Undefined / Unknown".
• The button "Write Secure Tokens"
◦ All secure tokens encapsulated in it can be extracted and written to the ECUs by pressing
this button. This causes the ECUs to switch to the desired ECU mode. The relevant
information is then updated in the SVT tree view in E-Sys.
SFA:
• The button “Read actual SFA state”
◦ In order to determine the status of all features (activated, deactivated, etc.) for each control
device shown in the SVT tree view, the user must press the "Read actual SFA state" button.
Communication with every SFA-capable ECU is started and its features are queried. The SVT
tree structure is then updated in E-Sys so that each ECU node can be opened and all existing
features can be displayed.
• The button "Create request file package for order"
◦ Similar to the button " Create request file Engineering Mode", the button " Create request file
package for order" can be used to create a request (JSON file) that can be subsequently sent
to the BMW backend system via B2B web application so that all required secure tokens for
restoring factory features can be calculated for all ECUs.
• The input field "File Name"
◦ A locally available response file downloaded via B2B web application, which contains the
required secure SFA tokens for control units, can be loaded into E-Sys → "File Name:" input
field.
• The button "Write SFA token"
◦ By pressing the "Write SFA token" button, the secure tokens are extracted from the JSON
response file and written to the ECUs concerned. The relevant information is then updated
in the SVT tree view in E-Sys.
• The button "incl. DELETE Token"
◦ The functionality "incl.DELETE Token" means that all active features that are no longer
available according to the target status are to be deleted (deactivated). If this is done, a new
secure token must be generated and imported if the feature is to be activated again at a later
point in time.

14.2. SFA/ECU-Mode Expert Mode
To call up the SFA and ECU mode modules in Expert Mode, press the "SFA / ECU-Mode Extended"
button on the left edge of the E-Sys.:
SFA / ECU-Mode Extended
A GUI interface is then displayed, which offers four tabs: “ECU-Mode”, “SFA”, “Token Management”
and “LCS”.
In contrast to the Comfort Mode, individual ECUs or groups of ECUs can now be selected for
treatment in the SVT tree view. For multiple selection, CTRL must be pressed while the individual
ECUs are selected from the SVT tree structure. By clicking on the first two lines ("SVT …", "SFAenabled ECUs") you can select all ECUs in the SVT tree view.

The multiple selection can be undone by deselecting all ECUs with the CTRL key
pressed or by clicking on the first two lines of the SVT tree view ("SVT …", "SFAenabled ECUs").
14.2.1. ECU-Mode tab
Ecu-Mode tab
The "Field Mode" button → switches all ECUs selected in the SVT tree view to field mode. As in
Comfort Mode, no secure tokens are required for this.
The selected SFA-capable ECUs can be switched to the respective mode by simply pressing the
“Plant Mode” or “Engineering Mode” buttons.
Communication with the BMW backend is completely transparent for the user, all necessary secure
tokens are obtained and imported into the ECUs.
All information is then updated in the SVT tree view in E-Sys.
129
 The online mode requires that the E-Sys client is in the BMW intranet!
As already described, a locally saved response file (JSON file with a Secure Token Set) can also be
loaded into E-Sys → "File Name:" input field.
The "Mode:" field then shows one of the following values: "Plant Mode", "Engineering Mode", "Field
Mode", "Mixed" or "Undefined / Unknown". As soon as the ECU-Mode Secure Token Set has been
loaded, all affected ECUs are highlighted in the SVT tree view.
All secure tokens contained in the Secure Token Set can be extracted by pressing the “Write Secure
Tokens” button and written to the relevant ECUs. This causes the ECUs to switch to the desired ECU
mode. All information is then updated in the SVT tree view in E-Sys. In order to determine the
currently active ECU mode for each selected ECU and to display it in the SVT tree view, the user
must press the {"Read ECU-Mode"} button.
Communication is started with the affected ECUs and their actual ECU modes are queried. The
relevant information is then updated in the SVT tree structure in E-Sys.
14.2.2. SFA tab
SFA tab
Online case:
 The online mode requires that the E-Sys client is in the BMW intranet!
By pressing the "Write SFA package for order" button, all features in the selected ECUs can be
restored to the original status that was defined in the factory for all SFA-capable ECUs.
Communication with the BMW backend is completely transparent for the user, all necessary secure
tokens are obtained and imported into the relevant ECUs. The relevant information is then updated
in the SVT tree view in E-Sys.
If a token recalculation is to be carried out online, the checkbox "incl. Token new calculation"
must be activated. The token recalculation means that a new token should also be generated for
target features that are already active on the vehicle.
130
The functionality "incl. DELETE Token" means that all active features that are no longer available
according to the target status are to be deleted (deactivated). If this is done, a new secure token
must be generated and imported if the feature is to be activated again at a later point in time.
Offline case:
A locally available JSON response file that is downloaded via a B2B web application and contains
secure SFA tokens can be loaded into E-Sys → "Secure Token Set file (JSON):“ input field.
By pressing the "Write SFA token" button, the secure tokens are extracted from the JSON response
file and written to the ECUs. The relevant information is then updated in the SVT tree view in E-Sys.
In order to determine the status of all SG features (activated, deactivated, etc.) for each selected
ECU, the user must press the "Read SFA status" button. Communication is started with the affected
ECUs and their features are queried. The relevant information is then updated in the SVT tree view
in E-Sys.
14.2.3. Token-Management tab
Token Management Tab
By pressing the "Create request file package for order " button, a request file for the SFA factory
state is created with or without recalculation of all SFA tokens.
By pressing the "Create request file Engineering Mode" and "Create request file Plant Mode"
131
buttons, a request file for secure tokens is created for switching selected ECUs to the "Engineering"
and "Plant" secure ECU modes.
By pressing the "Send token set to backend" button, a loaded request file is sent to the backend,
depending on the request type (Token for ECU modes, Package for Order, newest Package for
Order). If the request type is "newest Package for Order", the request file must contain the name
"newest".
By pressing the “Read SFA status” or “Read ECU-Mmode” buttons, the information that belongs to
the selected nodes in the SVT tree view can be updated.
By pressing the "Read Secure Token Details" button, a detailed display of information relating to
each selected ECU feature in the SVT tree view is initiated.
By pressing the "Read Import Status" button, the result of the last imported token is read. The
result is displayed in the status panel.
By clicking the "Delete Secure Token" button, the features selected in the SVT tree view are
deactivated and the associated secure SFA tokens are deleted.
By pressing the "Clear Secure Token" button, all of the features selected in the SVT tree view are
deactivated, but the associated secure SFA tokens are retained in the ECU ( later re-use is
possible!). Restriction: CLEARE_FEATURE is only possible for ECUs that are in engineering mode.
By pressing the "Verify Tokens and Vin" button, all secure SFA tokens that belong to the selected
ECU features in the SVT tree view are verified.
14.2.4. LCS tab
LCS Tab
132
Locking Configuration Switch (LCS) enables special configurations to be changed quickly.
One example is the secure bypass. An Activation is required if ECUs are installed in a vehicle that
communicates with each other, where some support secure communication (secure on-board
communication, SecOC) and others do not. A specific configuration can be selected using the dropdown menus under the label "LCS name:". The same can be achieved by directly entering a
corresponding two-digit hexadecimal number to the left of the menus.
A similar behaviour happens under the “LCS value” label: the user can type in a desired LCS value
or choose the predefined ones on the drop-down menus, which is written to all ECUs selected in the
SVT tree view after pressing the “Write LCS value” button.
By pressing the "Read LCS" button, LCS values for the specified configuration are queried for all
SFA-capable ECUs selected in the SVT tree view.
Alternatively, a file with LCS tokens can be used in the "Set LCS via a token" field to perform the LCS
switchover.
The checkbox in the "Set LCS" panel can be used to determine whether a reset should be carried
out after the LCS switchover.
14.2.5. IPSec-Deactivation
Tab IPSec-Deactivation
133
Control units with and without IPSec support can be installed in a vehicle. IPSec can be deactivated
for the IPSec-capable control units so that they can communicate with the IP control units. For this
purpose, the addresses must be known to the IPSec control units. This is done with the help of a bit
mask which can be generated and written at this point.
To write the bit mask, individual control units can be selected in the tree on the right. If no control
units are selected, the bit mask is written to all visible control units that support IPSec bit mask.
14.2.6. ECU-UID
Tab ECU-UID
In development, it is necessary to be able to import tokens to control units, for example to set a
control unit to engineering mode. These tokens are generated in the backend. Certain rights are
required for the generation of tokens, which are also dependent on the vehicle. Since there are no
vehicles in development, only ECUs, it is possible to register an ECU as a development part in the
backend.
134
In the "Register selected ECUs" panel, the registration can be carried out directly from E-Sys. The
prerequisite for the registration process is a connection to a vehicle and set BASIC login data. If
these prerequisites are met, the registration process can be triggered for all ECUs selected in the
SVT tree.
In the panel "Registration using an ECU list file" this registration process can be executed separately.
Via the button "Create ECU-List file" a JSON file is generated, which can then be used via the B2B
portal or also via E-Sys for the registration of developer parts.
A connection to the vehicle is also a prerequisite here, as ECU-specific information is to be read out.
In the panel "Registration using an existing ECU list file", the registration of development parts can
be triggered with an ECU list file (such as from the previous paragraph) via the button "Perform
registration".
Since this action involves communication with the SFA backend, prior specification of BASIC login
data is mandatory. A vehicle connection is not required, as all necessary data is contained in the
ECU list file.
14.2.7. Basic Security Features
In this tab the user can read basic features (i.e., Tokens, Certificates, CSR Keylist, SecOC, LCS, IPsec,
EAP and MACsec) of a list of ECUs. The results are displayed in the status panel.
14.2.8. ACL
In this tab the user can choose between 3 jobs:
Enable ACL and Disable ACL – Activates or deactivates the security feature ACL (Access Control
135
List) of the received.
This will return between one of the parameters: OK; ERROR; OPERATION_AREADY_RUNNING;
INVALID.
Read ACL - Reads the ACL state on the received ECUs
This will return between one of the parameters: ACTIVATED; DEACTIVATED; INVALID
14.3. SecOc Comfort Mode
To call up the SecOC in comfort mode, press the “SecOC” button on the left edge of the E-sys:
A GUI interface is then displayed which only offers one tab: “SecOC Update”.
In comfort mode, the functionalities are simplified and offered to a reduced extent. The main
feature is the SecOC keys value update, activation or deactivation. I.e., a selection of one or more
nodes in the SVT tree view is not possible in comfort mode. This is what is known as the “Whole
Vehicle Treatment”.
136
14.3.1. SecOC update tab
This tab allows the user to activate or deactivate SecOC keys.
To deactivate SecOC, the LCS #1 must be set to 1.
To activate SecOC, the LCS #1 must be set to the value 2 (partial on) or 5 (full), depending on the
service pack. The on-board network or the service pack (COM parameter SERVICE_PACK) of the
built-in SecOC Counter Master (COM parameter SECOC_COUNTER_MASTER=true) is decisive here.
In addition to the LCS #1, the LCS #0 (ServicePack) must also be switched to the correct service
pack.
