Chapter 15. Certificate Management
As an enabler for new functions and to increase the security of existing functions, individual
certificates are required when handling vehicles.
Therefore, as of SP2018, individual certificates and their binding to the respective vehicle must be
introduced in the factory as well as in the service. In addition, bindings must be distributed
between ECUs.
Before work can begin with certificate management, an SVT actual must first be loaded or read
from the vehicle:
Load SVT-Actual
E-Sys then creates an SVT tree view in the right-hand GUI area, in which all CertEnabled ECUs
found are displayed. At each ECU node, the information is also displayed: Base variant,
hexadecimal ECU address in square brackets and the Certificate version also in square brackets.
The second necessary step is to read out the VIN from the vehicle or, if SVT-Actual has been loaded
as a file, to enter it manually into the VIN input field. E-Sys also offers the user a comfort and an
expert mode for certificate management.
15.1. Certificate Management in Comfort Mode
To call up the SFA and ECU mode module in Comfort mode, press the "Certificate management"
button on the left side of E-Sys:
Module Certificate Management
A GUI interface is then displayed that offers only two tabs: "Online" and "Offline".
In the comfort mode, the functionalities are simplified and offered in a reduced scope.
139
The main feature is that certificate requests or request file creation is only possible at all ECUs
listed in the SVT tree view.
I.e. a selection of one or more nodes in the SVT tree view is not possible in Comfort mode. This is
the so-called "whole vehicle treatment".
15.1.1. Certificate Management Online
Certificate Management Comfort Online
In the "online" tab, the user is offered two actions. The first generates a request file for the vehicle,
sends it to the backend and writes the response to the ECUs. This functionality is triggered via the
button "Get and write data" and can only be used if the user is in the BMW intranet. In addition, a
client certificate must have been imported into E-Sys beforehand.
The button "Start data check" checks the status of the existing certificates, bindings, other bindings
and keys for the certificate-capable ECUs. The result of the individual ECUs is displayed in the SVT
tree. In addition, a result file is stored in the Cert folder.
The button "Read Status" will fetch for the ECU certificate status without a previous check as
supposed to. The results of this method could not be reliable since it will return in the worst-case
scenario the arbitrary result from a previous calculation which couldn’t be accurate.
15.1.2. Certificate Management Offline
Certificate Management Offline
140
In the "offline" tab, the user has the option to create a file with the individual certificate requests in
JSON format in the "Create CBB request file" panel. The user can then upload this file to the B2B
portal to get the response generated.
Alternatively, the user can also send the request file to the backend via the button "Send CBB
request file to backend" in this module. However, permission must first be granted for this.
In the "Write data" panel, a previously generated CBB response file can be selected and written to
the ECUs. If the ECUs also require otherBindings, these are automatically calculated and also
written to the corresponding ECUs.
The status of the existing certificates, bindings, otherBindings and keys is checked for the
certificate-capable ECUs via the "Start data check" button. The result of the individual ECUs is
displayed in the SVT tree. In addition, a result file is stored in the Cert folder.
15.1.3. SecureDiag
Certificate Management SecureDiag
141
15.1.3.1. Add Service29 certificate:
Retrieves Service29 Certificates from backend with the selected role. Needs strong authentication to
the Sec4Diag backend and the client certificate.
Can also import locally stored Service29 Certificates and store it in the user´s keystore.
15.1.3.2. Generate request for Service29 certificate:
Issues a certificate request for a given VIN with a chosen tester role mask and saves it in the default
CERT folder.
For convenience, user can print E-sys public key in the console.
15.1.3.3. Add TLS Test Certificate plus private key:
Adds the content of the selected certificate file and key file to the key store. Both files need to
contain the vehicle VIN and it needs to be the same in both vehicles.
142
15.1.3.4. Manage Certificates:
Check Certificates:
Prints all TLS certificates' VIN and expiration date to the logs.
Delete Expired Certificates:
Deletes all expired certificates from the TLS Key Store.
15.2. Certificate Management Expert Mode
To call up the SFA and ECU mode module in expert mode, press the "Certificate Management"
button on the left-hand E-Sys side:
Module Certificate Management Extended
In the Expert Module, in contrast to the Comfort Module, the user can also select individual ECUs in
the SVT tree.
As an enabler for new functions and to increase the security of existing functions, individual
Certificates are required in the treatment of vehicles. From SP2018, individual Certificates and their
binding to the respective vehicle must be installed both in the factory and in the service. In
addition, bindings between ECU devices must be distributed. This functionality is provided by this
module.

The functionalities provided in this module which include direct server access
require to have several preconditions to be fulfilled:
• The system which runs E-Sys must be in a BMW network segment in which the
backend systems (CBB) are available.
• There must be a valid E-Sys client Certificate imported into E-Sys.
• At least one URL of a valid backend system (CBB) must be configured in E-Sys.
A more detailed set of instructions can be found here: HOWTO (only available
within BMW network) - if the link does not automatically open, please validate your
Access Permissions to the shared folder and contact your BMW Contact Person.
For further questions please contact the support service: support-securitysystemfunktionen@bmw.de
15.2.1. Overview Certificate Management Module
The Certificate management module has 8 tabs. The individual functions are explained in the
following sections:
143
• Get, write, check and delete data
• Write data individually
• Read data individually
• Calculate OtherBinding (SP2018)
• Edit CBB-Transfer data
• SecOC
• IPSec
• MACSec
15.2.1.1. Get, write, check and delete data
Supports beside the functionality of the Certificate Management in Comfort Mode, this module
supports the possibility of filtering ECUs using black-lists and white-lists. These lists should contain
the comma-separated diagnostic addresses of the desired ECUs in hex format and are saved as a .txt
file.
For the whitelist it is also possible to select the desired ECUs in the displayed SVT.
Format of the blacklist: 0x63,0x61,0x60,… (comma-separated diagnostic addresses in hex format)
File-Type: <FILE_NAME>.txt (e.g. blacklist.txt)
The checkbox "Enable Restbus Keys" enables the storage of the symmetric keys of the ECUs in plain
text. If this option is selected, these keys are stored in an XML file. The path and name of this XML
file can be freely selected.
It is possible to use either a loaded file as white-list or just click at the ECUs you want to treat (in the
144
SVT view on the right). If no filter is selected all ECUs will be treated.
 It is not possible to have a loaded filter file and selected ECUs in the SVT view.
15.2.1.1.1. Simulation of residual bus
Checkbox 'Enable residual bus Keys' allows the storage of symmetrical keys for the ECUs in plain
text. With this option selected, the keys will be stored into XML-files. Name and path for the XMLfiles can be defined by the user.
Start data check
Performs the Certificates check of the ECUs. The result is logged in a local result-file as well as
displayed in the SVT view.
Read status
Read the ECUs certificate status. The result is logged in a local result-file as well as displayed in the
SVT view.
Check persistent certificates
Performs a check of persistently stored certificates and keys in the ECUs, if available. The results
are displayed in the status panel. Two types of checks can be performed:
• Quick: a fast/quick check
• Full: a complete check of certificates, including the certificates signatures
Create a local CSR-file
Generates an JSON request-file that can either uploaded in the B2B-portal to get the response or
send it trough E-Sys to the backend (only possible on the BMW-Intranet).
Delete certificates
• Delete Certificates - deletes the following data from ECUs:
◦ certificates and Keys
◦ all installed individual certificates
◦ all symmetric SecOC keys (if possible)
◦ the status of all individual certificates
◦ SecOC keys, as well as their overall status
• Delete Keys and Certificates - deletes the following data from ECUs:
◦ every keypair of all individual certificates (only in the development phase, as long as they
are not already stored in the HSM / SHE)
◦ every generated CSR
◦ the signatures of all generated CSRs
145
◦ every installed individual certificate
◦ the timestamp of the individual certificates, so older certificate can be installed
◦ the generated keylist
◦ the signature of the generated keylist
◦ the timestamp of the keypack - all symmetric SecOC keys
• Deletes Timestamps from Certificate and Keypacks - deletes the following data from ECUs:
◦ the timestamp of the individual certificates, so older certificate can be installed
◦ the timestamp of the keypack, so older keypacks can be installed
15.2.1.2. Write data individually
In this tab, the user has the option of writing the respective memory types individually to the
vehicle.
To be able to use the function, a valid XML file containing the type of memory object selected in the
table must be specified for the respective ECU in the table.
This is done via the button with the three dots in the "Load" column.
The actual writing process can then be initiated via the "Write" button.
 The data format of the loaded object is XML and not JSON. The response file can’t
be used in this slide.
Each ECU can only be written with one memory type (i.e., 1 or 2) at once.
Description of types: (numeric value)
Certificates / CSRs (Type 1): 0
Binding (Type 1): 1
OtherBindings: 2
Certificates / CSRs (Type 2): 3
Binding (Type 2): 4
Keylist: 5
146
15.2.1.3. Read data individually
Reads the selected Certificate type from the configured ECU devices and displays the result in the
status window.
This creates a file in XML format for each ECU to be handled, which contains the entire certificate
container of the respective ECU. The default storage location for this is the CERT directory in the ESys Data directory.
The possible selection options for the memory type are:
• CERTIFICATE
• BINDING
• OTHER_BINDING
• ONLINE_BINDING_ECU
• SEC_OC_KEYLIST
• MAC_SEC_KEYLIST
In the selected storage location, one or more XML files are now dependent on the selected memory
object type. For each ECU can only be read out on memory type at the time.
Example of stored XMLs:
• BindingContainer_<Basisvariante>_<DiagAdr[Hex]>_fromVehicle_<Timestamp>.xml
• CertificateContainer_<Basisvariante>_<DiagAdr[Hex]>_fromVehicle_<Timestamp>.xml
147
15.2.1.4. Calculate OtherBinding (SP2018)
A binding distribution can be created in this tab. However, this is only possible for certificatecapable ECUs with SP2018. In addition, the otherBinding file can be written to the vehicle in this tab
after generation.
The Binding Distribution contains the information about which ECUs are allowed to establish a
secure communication with each other.
The Calculate Distribution button calculates the OtherBindings, which contain the information
about which ECU devices may communicate with each other in the vehicle. For this purpose, the
user selects a location for the BindingDistribution file. The default storage location is the CERT
directory in the E-Sys Data directory. Here, the user has the possibility to influence the calculation
148
of the distribution with the checkboxes to the right of the files to be loaded.
Use case Result
Both check boxes active PSdZ calculates the OtherBindings by using the
bindings of the backend with the bindings from
the vehicle for calculation.
Checkbox from backend active and from vehicle
inactive
PSdZ does not get any readout binding set from
the vehicle to the calculation and only the
bindings from the backend will be transferred
for calculation.
Checkbox from vehicle active and from backend
inactive
PSdZ will only allow the bindings from the
vehicle to be included in the calculation and
only bindings from the vehicle will be used
accordingly.
Both check boxes inactive This combination does not provide a result since
no bindings are passed to PSdZ.

If BindingContainer is available from the CBB-Box and the vehicle for the same
control unit, the newly calculated container from the CBB-Box is always used
again. The container determined from the vehicle is discarded.
In the "Write OtherBindings to Vehicle" panel, the previously calculated OtherBindings can then be
written to the vehicle.
15.2.1.5. Edit CBB-Transfer data
In this tab, the user has the possibility to:
• Extract individual memory objects of the loaded JSON file and store them in a XML file.
• Delete individual Certificate roles from a CSR file
• Generate the request file with the loaded XML files
To extract the XML containers from the CBB response file, a JSON file must first be loaded in the
corresponding panel via the file selection field. Then the extraction can be started via the button
"Extract data".
The button "Delete certificate role" offers the function to delete the role selected in the drop-down
menu from the loaded JSON request file. After confirming the button, a separate XML file is created
for each memory object that was contained in the JSON file and saved locally. The selected role ID is
then no longer contained in the resulting files.
In the panel "CBB request file generation", an own request file can be assembled. Depending on the
loaded SVT, all certifiable ECUs are displayed in the table.
SP2021 ECUs are listed twice in the table. Once to load the CSR file and the second time to load the
key-packs (for secure onboard communication).
149
When all desired data has been loaded, the CBB file can be generated via the button "Generate file".
Extract XML files from JSON:
1. Load JSON file
2. Button Extract data
Delete role IDs:
1. Load request JSON file.
2. Chose role that you want to delete.
3. Button Delete Role
Create a CSR file:
1. Load or read SVT.
2. Load all the memory object [XML] in the table
5. Button Generate file
15.2.1.6. SecOC
The SecOC function is intended to ensure the integrity of messages exchanged between components
in the vehicle.
In this tab, the user is offered the following functions for Secure Onboard Communication:
Via the button "Read SecOC Master Counter", the SecOC counter of all ECUs selected in the SVT tree
can be read out if the connection to the vehicle is successful.
The results are displayed for each ECU in the status panel.
In the panel below, the button "Write SecOC Master Counter" can be used to enter a new SecOC
Counter value in the text field provided and then write it to all selected ECUs.
In addition, there is the option of reading the SecOC Master Counter value from the SecOC Master
150
ECU as well as writing a new value to it.
The SecOC master ECU is determined automatically.
A selection in the SVT tree is not necessary for this.
In the Read SecOC Details panel, the button Read SecOC Details is responsible for reading the SecOC
details from a SecOC enabled ECU.
These details include the SecOC status, the Keypack status and the keypack creation time status.
In this tab, the user has the possibility to:
• Read out the current SecOC counter value of all selected ECUs.
• Set a new SecOC counter value to all selected ECUs.
• Read out the current SecOC Master counter value of the SecOC Master ECU. The SecOC Master
ECU will be determined automatically - no selection in SVT-Tree required.
• Set a new SecOC Master counter value to the SecOC Master ECU. The SecOC Master ECU will be
determined automatically - no selection in SVT-Tree required.
• Read the state of the SecOC. This includes the SecOC status, the key pack status, the key pack
creation time status, the LCS1 current status, the response status and the ECU unknown status.
• Read the SecOC Details. This includes SecOC status, the keypack status and the keypack creation
time status
The result is shown in the status panel.
 • These actions can only be performed on ECUs that support this functionality.
151
• The ECUs must be in engineering ECU Mode (applicable to write operations).
• Text fields accept values in HEX in the range [0x0 .. 0xFFFFFFFF].
15.2.1.7. IPSec
In this tab, all IPSec-capable ECUs can be activated, deactivated, locked or get the status read.

• The following command can only be performed on ECUs that are
• For each action, all IPSec-capable ECUs are addressed. This means that the
selection in the SVT tree is not considered.
15.2.1.8. MACSec
MACSec of all MACSec-enabled ECUs can be activated, deactivated, locked or read in this tab.
MACSec is a security function to provide security on the Ethernet Layer 2. The goal on the Ethernet
cable is to protect the integrity of the transferred data from one ECU to another
152

• The following command can only be performed on ECUs that support this
functionality.
• For each action, all MACSec-enabled ECUs are handled. Selection in the SVT
tree is not considered.
15.3. Batch
Batch functionality for this section is described in detail at Certificate Management.
153
Chapter 16. Anflash
During vehicle assembly, the possibility was created to perform a so called Anflash operation in ESys. It is based on scripts and makes it possible to bring several ECUs sequentially from their initial
state to a defined target state in E-Sys.
E-Sys takes the necessary information from configuration files. During the process, a separate
report is generated for each ECU handled. At the end of the processing, the overall result of the
flash process is summarized in an overall report.
For the Anflash process, a Master Config file must first be created.
16.1. Creation of a master config file
Anflash editor module
New master config files can be created and existing ones edited in the Anflash Editor module.
16.1.1. Create Master Config
A new master config is created via the menu item 'File New' or the corresponding icon in the menu
bar:
Anflash editor - 'New' menu item
154
After pressing the menu option 'New' a new Master-Config object is created and displayed.
 This object is not yet saved as a file!
16.1.2. Save generated master config
After editing the missing entries, the newly created master config can be saved as a file via the
menu item 'File Save as…'.
Anflash editor - 'Save as…' menu item
16.1.3. Edit Master Config entries
The user has the possibility to edit the following entries in the Master-Config:
• FA: FA file with path specification (absolute or relative).
• ECU Root: Directory where the ECU-Config files are located (absolute or relative).
• ECU-CONFIG: Name of the ECU-Config files. (All ECU-Config files must be located in the ROOTFOLDER directory).
If connection parameters are defined in the master config file (these are only required in batch
mode), it is not possible to change these parameters. There is also no representation of these
parameters. These values are neither changed nor deleted when editing and saving the file.
155
16.1.3.1. Edit FA entry
FA entries can be specified with both absolute and relative paths.
Anflash editor - FA entry
When selecting an FA file via the 'Load' button, the path specification is displayed absolutely.
Relative path specifications can be defined by editing the text field. The 'Reset' button ensures that
the FA entry that was last saved in the master config is restored.
16.1.3.2. Edit ECU root entry
The ECU root directory, where all ECU-Config files are located, can be specified with absolute or
relative path.
Anflash editor - ECU root entry
Via the button 'Load' an ECU root directory can be determined via a selection menu. In this case, the
path is displayed as an absolute value. A relative path specification can be realized by editing the
text field. The 'Reset' button restores the ECU root entry that was last saved in the master config.
16.1.3.3. Edit ECU Config entries
The ECU-Config names displayed in a tree structure can be edited in the following ways:
• Delete entry
• Rename entry
• Add new entry
• Change the order of the entries
Deleting an entry is done by selecting the corresponding entry and choosing the context menu item
'Delete':
Anflash Editor - Delete ECU Config Entry
156
To rename an entry, this entry is first marked. After a double click a text field opens in which a new
name for this config file can be entered:
Anflash Editor - Rename ECU Config entry
To add a new entry, the root node 'ECU-CONFIG' must be selected and the corresponding context
menu 'Add Ecu-Config' must be executed:
Anflash Editor - Add ECU Config Entry
The order of the ECU Config entries can be defined by moving the tree elements. For this purpose,
any node is marked and moved to the desired position in the tree:
Anflash Editor - Setting the Order of the ECU Config Entry
157
16.1.4. Save changes
After changes have been made to the master config, they can be saved. For this purpose, the user
can either use the menu item 'File Save ' or the corresponding icon in the menu bar:
Anflash editor - 'Save' menu item
16.2. Overview of configuration files
16.2.1. Master Config File
The contents of the Master Config file can be divided into three groups:
• Connection Parameters (Connection Properties)
• FA specification
• Definition of the ECUs to be treated
16.2.1.1. FA specification
In order to execute a TAL, it is mandatory to specify a vehicle order (FA). Since all TAL-Config files
to be processed must contain the same FA, this property is managed centrally in the Master-Config.
FA = <FA filename>
The path to the FA file can be specified both absolutely and relatively. If you specify a relative path,
the reference point is the directory in which the master config file is stored.
Example 1:
FA specification (with absolute path):
C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/FaData/FA-S15C.xml
Example 2:
Storage location for the master config file:
C:/Temp/Config
158
FA specification (with relative path):
../../FaData/FA-S15C.xml
Absolute path to the FA file:
C:/FaData/FA-S15C.xml
Example 3:
Storage location for the master config file:
C:/Temp/Config
FA specification (with relative path):
/FaData/FA-S15C.xml
Absolute path to the FA file:
C:/Temp/Config/FaData/FA-S15C.xml
16.2.1.2. ECU-Config Definitions
ECU-Config files are used to edit individual ECUs. These are to be defined in the master config file as
follows:
• ROOT_FOLDER = <root directory where all ECU-Config files are located>.
• ECU_CONFIG_1 = < Config file for the first ECU to be edited>.
• ECU_CONFIG_2 = < Config file for the second ECU to be edited>.
• …
• ECU_CONFIG_n = < Config file for the nth ECU to be edited>.
Analogous to the path specification for the vehicle order, the specification for the ROOT_FOLDER
entry can be both absolute and relative.
Example 1:
ROOT_FOLDER = C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/Config
ECU_CONFIG_1 = BDC_64.config
ECU_CONFIG_2 = DCS_69.config
ECU_CONFIG_3 = SRR_8.config
159
This defines the following ECU-Config files:
C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/Config/BDC_64.config
C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/Config/DCS_69.config
C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/Config/SRR_8.config
Example 2:
ROOT_FOLDER = /EcuConfig
ECU_CONFIG_1 = BDC_64.config
ECU_CONFIG_2 = DCS_69.config
If the corresponding master-config file is located in the directory
'C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/Config'
then the following ECU-Config files are referenced via the settings in this example:
C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/Config/EcuConfig/BDC_64.config
C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/Config/EcuConfig/DCS_69.config
16.2.2. ECU Config file
In an ECU-Config file the following information must be set:
BASE_VARIANT = <base variant of the ECU to be used>.
DIAG_ADR = <diagnostic address of the ECU to be used>.

Care must be taken to ensure that the combination of base variant and diagnostic
address is unique. This means that a particular combination may only be used
once in all ECU-Config files.
KC_LIST = <list of containers to import; separated by semicolon>.
TAL_LIST = <list of TAL-Config files to be executed; separated by semicolon>.
Alternatively, the KC and TAL lists can also be specified with indices. If indices are used, then a TAL
list with the same index must also be defined for each KC list:
KC_LIST_1 = <list of containers to be imported first; separated by semicolon>.
TAL_LIST_1 = <list of TAL-Config files to be executed first; separated by semicolon>.
KC_LIST_2 = <list of containers to be imported second; separated by semicolon>.
160
TAL_LIST_2 = <list of TAL-Config files to be executed second; separated by semicolon>.
...
KC_LIST_n = <list of containers to be imported last; separated by semicolon>.
TAL_LIST_n = <list of TAL-Config files to be executed last; separated by semicolon>.
Both the paths to the containers to be imported and to the TAL-Config files can be absolute or
relative. With a relative path specification, the reference point is the directory in which the ECUConfig file is located.
Example:
BASE_VARIANT = BDC
DIAG_ADR = 32
KC_LIST_1 = C:/EC-Apps/Data/ODX/PT01_template.003_024_000.pdx
TAL_LIST_1 = /TalExecution/Tal1.config; C:/EC-Apps/Data/TalExecution/Tal2.config
KC_LIST_2 = C:/EC-Apps/Data/ODX/Test.003_024_001.pdx
TAL_LIST_2 = ../Data/TalExecution/Tal3.config
16.2.3. TAL-Config file
In the TAL-Config files, which are to be specified in the ECU-Configs under TAL_LIST, the following
parameter must be set obligatorily:
TAL = <TAL filename>
The path to the TAL file can be specified both absolutely and relatively. If the path is relative, the
reference point is the directory in which the TAL-Config file is located.
Example 1: TAL specification (with absolute path):
TAL = C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/TalData/tal-example1.xml
Example 2: TAL specification (with relative path):
TAL = /TalData/tal-example2.xml
If the TAL-Config file is located in the directory 'C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash',
then the absolute path to the TAL file results:
C:/EC-Apps/Batchmode/Anflash/TalData/tal-example2.xml
The following parameters can be used optionally:
• SVT
161
SVT = <SVT filename>
• CODING_type
◦ fa|shipment|ncd (Default: fa)
CODING_TYPE = <coding type>
• NCD_LIST
◦ optional path specification where the NCDs are located
◦ format <NCD path 1>;<NCD path 2>… , z.B.
"C:/NCD/00001234_0000dddd.caf.026_000_002.ncd;C:/NCD/00012345_0000bbbb.caf.006_011_0
08.ncd"
◦ Is only taken into account with coding type "ncd".
 only one control unit may be handled during NCD coding.
NCD_LIST = <NCD path 1>;
• USE_LOCAL_NCD
◦ Perform FA coding locally
◦ on|off OR true|false
USE_LOCAL_NCD = on
• PATH_NCD
◦ optional path where the NCDs are located, attention: in this directory a subfolder is searched
with the VIN as name
◦ If omitted, the NCD directory specified in the settings will be used. (stored in properties)
◦ Only considered for coding type "fa" and "shipment".
PATH_NCD = C:/signedNCD/
• PARALLEL_PROGRAMMING
◦ on|off
PARALLEL_PROGRAMMING = off
• CHECK_PROGRAMMING_COUNTER
162
◦ on|off
CHECK_PROGRAMMING_COUNTER = on
• REPEATS_ON_ERROR
REPEATS_ON_ERROR = <number of repetitions in case of error>.
• EVENT
◦ off|all|progress|transaction|error|tal|aep
EVENT= <event filter for console output>.
• FILL_INSTALLED_ECU_LIST
◦ on|off
FILL_INSTALLED_ECU_LIST = on
• FILL_INSTALLED_ECU_LIST_MODE
◦ merge|overwrite
FILL_INSTALLED_ECU_LIST_MODE = <mode how to fill the InstalledECUList>.
• MODE_SWITCH_PROGRAMMING
◦ on|off
MODE_SWITCH_PROGRAMMING = <mode switch on programming on/off>.
• GATEWAYS_TO_SWITCH_TO_PROGRAMMING_MODE
◦ List of gateways (diagnostic addresses in HEX) to be switched to programming mode.
◦ Without the parameter all available gateways will be switched.
◦ Ex: 10, 63
GATEWAYS_TO_SWITCH_TO_PROGRAMMING_MODE = <gateway list>
• TAL_FILTER
◦ Absolute or relative path to a TAL filter file.
◦ The path to a TAL filter file can be specified both absolutely and relatively. If the path is
163
relative, the reference point is the directory in which the TAL-Config file is located.
TAL_FILTER = <TAL filter filename>
• IDR_BACKUP_PATH
◦ Absolute path to a backup directory with individual data.
IDR_BACKUP_PATH = <IDR backup directory>
• READ_MILEAGE_FROM_GWSZ
◦ on|off
◦ If the parameter is on, the km status is read out before the TAL processing and written to
Fingerprint).
READ_MILEAGE_FROM_GWSZ = off
• MILEAGE
◦ 0-655330
MILEAGE = Km level for fingerprint
• HDD_UPDATE_SERVER_URL
◦ URL of the HDD update server
HDD_UPDATE_SERVER_URL = <URL for HDD update>
• ROE_DEACTIVATION
◦ on|off
◦ (Enable/disable response on event during TAL processing).
ROE_DEACTIVATION = off
• PREVENT_HTTP_TRANSMISSION
◦ on|off
◦ Prevent Http transfer protocol during TAL processing).
PREVENT_HTTP_TRANSMISSION = off
164
• OPTIMIZABLE_BOOTLOADER_FLASH
◦ on|off
◦ (Perform optimized bootloader flash on ECUs that support this functionality).
OPTIMIZABLE_BOOTLOADER_FLASH = off
• EXPECTED_SGBMID_VALIDATION
◦ on|off (perform check of expected Sgbmids)
EXPECTED_SGBMID_VALIDATION = on
NOTES:
• The specification of a FA is not required in this TAL configuration file. This specification is
obtained from the master config file.
• To process a TAL with coding actions (coding TAs), it is mandatory to specify an FA in the master
config file. Applies to CODING_TYPE = fa or shipment.
• With CODING_TYPE = ncd it is possible to create a SG with an already existing NCD file. encode.
The NCD_LIST option is mandatory.
• With CODING_TYPE = ncd only one control unit may be coded during a TAL processing.
• If the configuration file contains the parameter HDD_UPDATE_SERVER_URL, an HDD update is
performed, otherwise a TAL processing.
• For the switches (PARALLEL_PROGRAMMING, CHECK_PROGRAMMING_COUNTER,
FILL_INSTALLED_ECU_LIST) the values on and off can be defined.
• As default value for the parameters the values from the file Esys.properties are used.
• Do not use '\' in the configuration file. Instead, use '/' or '\' for path specifications.
16.3. Anflash process
16.3.1. Call in the user interface
In order to execute a complete flash cycle in GUI mode in a fully automated way, the following must
be set in the Anflash module:
• A valid master config file must be loaded. If necessary, the loaded file can be opened and
revised via the 'Edit' button in the Anflash Editor module (see previous chapter).
Anflash module
165
A prerequisite for the execution of the Anflash process is a valid vehicle connection. In addition, it
is checked before the Anflash process whether all required config files exist.
After a successful start all ECU-Configs defined in the Master-Config are processed sequentially in
the order of their position numbers.
During processing, the current process step is displayed and the "In progress" status is visualized by
the progress indicator. In the case of a TAL processing, the remaining processing time is also
displayed.
Anflash module - progress bar
The Anflash process can be aborted during execution via the Stop button. However, the action
currently being performed must be completed first.
After all control units have been treated, the progress display is highlighted in color depending on
the overall status:
• Green - Finished
• Orange - FinishedWithWarning
• Red - FinishedWithError, AbortedByUser, Exception
Additionally, all report files are generated Report generation.
16.3.2. Program sequence
It is first checked whether:
166
• a valid Master Config file is open
• at least one ECU-Config is marked for execution
• there is a connection to the vehicle
The FA and the ECU-Config files are read from the Master-Config. If connection parameters are
specified in the master config, these are ignored (these are only required in batch mode).
It also checks if all specified ECU-Config files exist and if they are valid.
After that, the information is read from the ECU-Config files.
It is checked whether all files specified in the config files exist (FA, PDX, TAL-Config and TAL).
If required files are missing, a list of all missing files is displayed and the Anflash process is
aborted.
It is checked whether the content of the specified TAL-Config files is valid.
If TAL-Config files with incorrect content exist, a listing of all incorrect files is displayed and the
Anflash process is aborted.
Data of the currently existing connection is remembered, and this connection is disconnected
A BAT-HAF test is performed once. In contrast to the batch mode, the behavior in case of a failed
check is not defined by a parameter, but by a user dialog. The user must decide in this dialog
whether he wants to continue the Anflash process or not.
The following steps are performed for each control unit to be processed:
• Import of component containers
• Establish connection to control unit
• Process TAL-Config files
• Close connection
After all the required steps for an ECU are completed, the final status is displayed in the table and a
corresponding ECU report is generated.
After all control units have been treated, an overall status is displayed, and a final overall report is
generated.
The original connection to the vehicle is restored.
16.3.3. BAT-HAF check
16.3.3.1. Background
The BAT-HAF control unit is used to ensure the power supply of critical systems in the vehicle.
Safety and driving-relevant control units are connected redundantly to a separate power supply
(secondary on-board power supply).
167
Primary and secondary supplies can be separated by a switch S1, which is integrated in the BATHAF. Another switch S2 enables the separation of the secondary supply from the secondary battery.
In normal operation both switches are closed.
From a certain voltage difference between primary and secondary network, S1 is automatically
opened and the secondary network is only supplied via the secondary battery. If this is the case at
the start of a flash process, excessive discharge of the secondary battery during the flash process
may cause switch S2 to open, which in turn would lead to flash aborts.
Since flash aborts can lead to undefined states of the control units or even defects, this risk should
be minimized as far as possible.
For this reason, a check of the switch state S1 has been integrated in E-Sys up from version 3.40.0.
Before the actual flash process is carried out, it is now checked whether switch S1 is open or closed.
16.3.3.2. Requirements for performing the test
During the execution of the -anflash command or when the process is started in the user interface,
one or more TAL files are executed.
Before each TAL execution, a test of the S1 switch takes place as soon as the following conditions
are met:
1. A BAT-HAF control unit must be installed in the vehicle. Identified by any of the below
conditions:
◦ EE Component with "BAT-HAF" description TalExecution.doS1Verification
◦ NameBNTN with "BAT-HAF" description.
◦ Diagnostic Address hex offset value as 31.
◦ Diagnostic Address offset value as 49.
2. The TesterApplyIdentifier (TEK) in E-Sys has a value not equal to 0xF.
3. If the TEK value is 0xF, then the execution of the check depends on a setting in the
Esys.properties file:
◦ TalExecution.doS1Verification=true → Verification is performed
◦ TalExecution.doS1Verification=false → Verification is not performed
The TalExecution.doS1Verification property can be changed via the settings dialog in E-Sys:
Settings/Options dialog - Perform S1 check
168
16.3.3.3. Successful check
If it is detected during the execution of the test that the S1 switch is closed, the flash process can be
carried out as usual. In this case, no action on the part of the user is required.
16.3.3.4. Meaning of the status values
The following table lists the different status codes:
Status code Meaning
0x00 Switch S1 is closed. Primary and secondary on-board power supply are
coupled.
0x01 The switch S1 is open. However, closing S1 is not problematic.
0x02 Switch S1 is open. However, closing of S1 is not possible due to an error
0x03 The switch S1 is open. Closing S1 is not possible as this would lead to a
crash.
0x04 Reserved return value
0x07 The command is temporarily open per diagnostics
0x08 The command is temporarily closed by diagnostics
0x09 The command is permanently open via the diagnosis
0x10 The command is permanently closed via the diagnostics
169
Status code Meaning
0xFF Invalid value.
16.3.4. Report generation
All generated reports are stored in a common directory.
For this purpose, each time the Anflash command is executed, a directory with the current
timestamp in the format yyyymmdd_hhmmss_SSS is created in the E-Sys Data directory below the
'Anflash_Reports' folder:
Anflash reports - folder structure
In this folder, a separate report is stored for each treated control unit.
Additionally, there is a report with the overall result of the Flash actions.
The report for the overall result is always stored under the following name:
OVERALL_RESULT_<yymmdd_hhmmss>.txt
The report names for the partial results of the individual control units are formed according to the
following scheme:
<base-variant>_<diagnostic-address>_RESULT_<yymmdd_hhmmss>.txt
Examples:
170
OVERALL_RESULT_210330_070000.txt
BDC_BODY3_64_RESULT_210330_071017.txt

The specifications for <base variant> and <diagnostic address> are taken from the
settings in the ECU-Config files.
16.3.5. Batch
Batch functionality for this section is described in detail at Anflash.
171
Chapter 17. FSC
This chapter describes E-Sys support for FSC (activation codes).
17.1. FSC comfort mode
The module FSC serves for inquiring the FSC’s state and for writing the FSC into ECU. In addition to
that it’s possible to (de)activate FSC’s already existing in the ECU. Only an activated FSC can really
be used.
Corresponding to the topic FSC there are other masks in E-Sys: FSC’s can be displayed and edited in
Edit Activation Codes (FSC) easily. In expert mode FSC-Extended-Module is available in addition to
that.
17.1.1. GUI Elements

Software-ID Identifier of software
Base Variant Name of ECU variant
Upgrade Index FSC’s index
172

Write FSC The FSC loaded into E-Sys is written to the ECU.
Update FSC The written FSC (to ECU) is checked and
activated.
Upgrade FSC Combines write FSC and update FSC.
Deactivate FSC Deactivate FSC in ECU (set to invalid)
17.2. FSC Extended
The module FSC Extended in expert mode serves for read out, check and sign of FSC. In addition to
that, single jobs can be executed in batch mode.
Corresponding to the topic FSC there are other masks in E-Sys. The module FSC comfort mode
serves for inquiring the FSC State, for writing and (de-)activating of FSC. FSC’s can be displayed and
edited in Edit Activation Codes (FSC) easily.

to the right hand window.

Chapter 18. Editors
18.1. Working in editors/viewers
18.1.1. Overview
In E-Sys there are various editors with which special file types can be edited. The following editors
are available:
Editor Description
FA Editor Processing of vehicle orders (FA)
TAL Editor Editing of Transaction Lists (TAL)
SVT Editor Editing of system variant tables (SVT)
SWESEQ Editor Editing SWE sequences (programming sequence)
FSC Editor Processing of activation codes (FSC)
FDL Editor Editing of function data lists (FDL)
In addition, there are viewers that are intended to display other file types but do not offer the
possibility to change them.
Viewer Description
CAF Viewer View Coding Application Files (CAF)
Log viewer Viewing log files (logs)
TALSTATUS viewer Evaluation of TAL processing
18.1.2. Working notes for tree views
Many editors use tree structures to display and edit hierarchical data. These offer the advantage of
good clarity and high flexibility.
Example editor with editing tree (FA editor)
175
The use follows the same concept at all points. The data is displayed and can usually be edited
directly, as far as this is provided for.
In general, the "leaves" of a tree, i.e. the concrete data, can be edited as follows:
• Triple click on the value
• Highlight the value and press the F2 key (function keys in the upper section of the keyboard).
• Edit in the context menu:
Clicking on a tree element with the right mouse button opens a context menu with editing options.
On node elements (folder symbol) sub-elements can often be inserted. On leaves (concrete values),
values can often be edited, deleted, etc.
Example of a context menu in an editor tree
176
Adjustable values have data types that require certain inputs. The values are checked when they
are entered (Enter key, click on another element). If they do not correspond to the default, they are
displayed with a red frame and must be corrected.
The following value types can occur:
Value type Example
Number 123, 456…
Text "AAG2", "HU"…
Date "27.01.2023"
List "true"/"false", "AAG2, CCU3" as drop-down element
18.2. Create and edit SVTs
SVT means "System Variant Table" and maps the composition of the installed control units with all
their parameters. For many functions, E-Sys requires the SVT target, which represents the target
state of the vehicle, or the SVT actual, which represents the current state of the vehicle.
In the SVT editor under Editors & Viewers, new SVTs can be created or existing ones edited.
The PSdZ can generate a TAL based on SVT-Actual and SVT-Target. This TAL contains the action list
to transform the vehicle from actual to reference state.

Whereas an SVT contains the state for a vehicle in the SVK (system installation
identifier) only the state of a single ECU is recorded. Therefore, an SVT consists of
at least one SVK. Since an SVK can be displayed as an SVT with a single SVK no
separate SVK-Editor exists.
177
18.2.1. Create SVT
There are several ways to create an SVT in E-Sys. This is possible by reading out, by creating a new
SVT or by editing an existing SVT. The last two points are explained below.
18.2.1.1. Create new SVT
A completely empty SVT can be created via the "File" menu or via the corresponding button in the
area below.
Create new SVT
18.2.1.2. Edit existing SVT
To edit an existing SVT (SVT actual), it can simply be loaded via the "…" button. button. If there is no
suitable SVT yet, it can be read out, for example, via the comfort module "TAL-Calculation".
SVT Actual loading
178
18.2.2. Edit SVT
The components of the system variant table (SVT) are displayed in a tree. The data can be adjusted
in the various sections of the tree.
18.2.2.1. Header
The top element is the "Header", in which meta information can be stored, such as creation time
and VIN.
SVT header
18.2.2.2. SVT
The individual components are listed below this node. A version number can be entered in the
node itself.
Standard SVT node
18.2.2.3. IdentifierHO or ECU
In the following level, a single "IdentifierHO" can be entered and any number of ECU components.
Each ECU is represented with its designation and the hex value of the diagnostic address. In the
example "AAG2" with diagnostic address "01":
Example ECU in the SVT editor "AAG2"
179
Existing ECUs can be changed as desired. If a new ECU is entered via the context menu, it initially
only receives a number as an identifier, e.g. "01". The name of the ECU is set automatically as soon
as a basic variant is entered.
The ECU can contain the setting categories listed in the following table:
Categories in "ECU"
GatewayDiagnosticAddress
ecuBusConnectionInfo
ecuDiagBusConnectionInfo
ecuDetailInfo
ComparisonInfo
PdxInfos
SmAcMasterSVK
18.2.3. SVT with SmAcs
Although Smart Actuators (SMACs) in SVT are on the same level as normal ECUs, they are
represented in a more user-friendly way in the SVT Editor. All SMACs are assigned to the related
Smart Actuator Master (SMAC Master) to allow a clearer representation of the mapping.
180
Smart Actuators in SVT
Adding new SMAC nodes is done via the item in the context menu of the respective SMAC master.
The new SMAC node is automatically assigned a valid diagnostic address when it is added (the first
2 digits correspond to the diagnostic address of the SMAC master).
If a change to the master results in SMACs being removed from the SVT, a confirmation prompt
appears via a dialog to the user, who can either confirm or cancel this.
181
18.3. FA/FP Edit
The module FA/FP-Editor displays and allows the edition of FAs (vehicle orders) and the
correspondent FPs (vehicle profiles). The FA designates a discrete state of installation of SWEs and
HWEs for a vehicle. You can derive the vehicle profiles from the vehicle order.
An ECU or a vehicle can contain/save exactly one vehicle order. During the communication with an
ECU or with a vehicle over PSdZ only a single vehicle order is exchanged. But in the local file system
a vehicle order is always saved within a list consisting of any number of vehicle jobs marked by a
unique ID.
182
18.3.1. Load FA
To display and edit, a FA can first be loaded from a local file. This is done via the "…" button next to
the file name, the corresponding icon in the toolbar or via the File/Open menu.
Alternatively, an ISTA-P file can also be imported, via the import icon in the toolbar or also via the
menu File/FA-Import ISTAP→PSDZ.
FA Loading
After loading, the content of the FA is displayed in the hierarchical tree below and the vehicle
profile is determined on the right-hand side.
18.3.2. Create new FA
It is also possible to create a completely new FA, this is possible via the New button or via the File
/New menu.
Create new FA
183
In this case, the following elements must be entered as mandatory:
• Entwicklungsbaureihe (Development series)
• Lackcode (Lacquer code)
• Polstercode (Upholstery code)
• Typschlüssel (Type key)
• Zeitkriterium (Time criterion)
18.3.3. Edit and save FA
The FA node contains general meta-information. The FZAuftrag node begins with a Header in
which, for example, the creation time and VIN of the order can be set.
Under Type you will find the specific details of the vehicle, for example the development series.
Other important node elements are:
Node Description
E-Wort Specific vehicle components relevant to the development stage
("HUDM", "HUEN" …)
HO-Wort Indication of the trader organisation (1-5 characters)
SALAPA-Element Items of optional equipment ("255", "2TB"…)
Table 15: Important information in the FA Editor
There is a separate editing area directly under the tree especially for the SALAPA-Element node.
There, the values can be entered directly and continuously. Changes must be confirmed with the
button on the right in the area title in order to be adopted in the tree.
As soon as a FA has been changed or newly created, it can be saved. It can be saved either in the
regular E-Sys format or as an ISTA-P export.
For this purpose, three commands are available in the File menu (Save, Save as, FA-Export
PSDZ→ISTAP) and two corresponding buttons in the toolbar.

18.4. Edit SWE sequences (SWESEQ)
Some ECUs require a certain sequence to be followed in order to flash their software units (SWE)
correctly.
To make this possible, SWE sequences can be set up for precise control. Here, the SWE flash order
can be precisely defined.
After completing the SWESEQ configuration, the result file can be imported into the configuration
part of a PDX container.
The following explains how to load and create the SWESEQ configuration. To do this, start the
SWESEQ Editor module under Editors & Viewers.
185
18.4.1. Load SWE sequences
An existing SWESEQ file can be loaded via the Open button or via the File/Open menu.
Load SWE sequences
After loading, the content of the file can be viewed and edited.
18.4.2. Create new SWE sequences
To create a new SWE sequence manually, the New button or the menu item File/New can be used.
186
Create new SWESEQ
After creation, the content of the file can be viewed and edited.

The values of the SWESEQ file are displayed as a tree. A version number can be entered in the
upper area.
Example SWE sequence
The node "EcuDependencies" is intended for the dependencies of the individual SWEs.
18.4.3.1. Edit SWE sequences
Software units relevant to sequences can be added via the context menu.
Insert SWE into sequence
187
Each entry requires a bootloader ID as well as the selection of a base variant and the entry of a

One or more bootloader IDs, which must be processed before the current SWE, must be entered

Similarly, all bootloader IDs that depend on the current SWE are entered under the "Dependors"
node.
18.4.3.2. Save SWE sequences

toolbar or the menu items "Save" or "Save as…".

sweseq_<bootloader-ID>.xml.<version 1st part>_<version 2nd part>_<version 3rd part>
Save SWE sequence
After saving the SWESEQ file, it can be transferred into a PDX container.
18.5. Edit Activation Codes (FSC)
Module FSC Editor serves for displaying and modifying FSCs.
Activation Codes are 20-digit character combinations that can be used to unlock specific functions
in the vehicle (e.g. navigation).
Corresponding to the topic FSC there are other modules in E-Sys: Module FSC comfort mode serves
for inquiring the FSC State, for writing and (de-)activating of FSC. In expert mode the FSC Extended
188
is available in addition to that.
18.5.1. Download FSC
An FSC file can be loaded via the "…" button or the File/Open menu.
Loading FSC
The loaded values are then displayed in the tree.
18.5.2. Create new FSC
An FSC file can be created via the "New" button in the toolbar.
Create new FSC
The values can then be edited. The following minimum values are required:
• Version
• FGN kurz (FGN short)
• Requester ID
189
18.5.3. Edit FSC
The unlock codes can be created so that they are dependent on certain conditions, e.g., the number
of operating hours, or the mileage.
To create a validity condition, a group is first added via the context menu of the Validity Conditions
node. Up to five types of conditions can then be added below the group.
• AllGB – Betriebsstunden Interval (Operating hours)
• AllGB – Ablaufdatum (Expiry date)
• AllGB – Kilometerintervall (Mileage)
• AllGB – Unbegrenzte Gültigkeitsbedingung (Unlimited)
• AllGB – Zeitraum (Period)
Editing activation codes
After or during the changes, it can be checked whether the data correspond to the validation
specification. To do this, click the Validate button in the lower operating area.
Validate FSC data
190
18.5.4. FSC sign, check signature
The processed FSC data can be provided with a cryptographic signature. Likewise, any existing
signature of an FSC file can be checked for validity.
For this purpose, there is an option in the lower operating area to load a key file ("…" button).
Sign FSC file, check signature
The Sign button can be used to sign the file loaded in the upper area. With Validate signature, an
already existing signature is checked for validity and a corresponding message is given.
18.6. View CAFs (Coding Application Files)
A CAF file is a special software unit (SWE) that contains coding data for a single control unit. It is
also possible to use several CAFs for one control unit. To edit CAFs, the CAF Viewer module can be
started under Editors & Viewers.
To open a CAF file, the menu File/Open or Recent Files can be used. Alternatively, the button from
the toolbar or the "…" button next to the field for the loaded file name can also be used.
Open CAF
After opening, the coding data is displayed as a tree structure. It is divided into individual coding
data groups within a CAF file. Each data group contains at least one function with at least one
parameter each.
Overview CAF Viewer
191
A user can look for a value in the CAF data using the search function. If an elemental is found, it
will be shown in the tree and if it is necessary, the tree will be opened.
The checkboxes Delivery Values and Parameter control whether the initial default values should be
visible in the tree.
18.7. Edit function data lists (FDL)
A function data list is a CAF (Coding Application File) which is enriched with data actually present
in the ECU. While a CAF exists as a data set before an ECU coding, an FDL is created by reading data
from an ECU and entering it into the corresponding CAF.
First, an existing NCD file is loaded, which was created in the NCD Preparation module, for
example.
Open NCD file
192
After loading an NCD file, the content is displayed in a tree structure. Below CAF, the content is
divided into headers and data.
Meta information is displayed in the header, e.g.
• Allgemein (General data, e.g. creator, date)
• CAF-Identifikator (CAF identifier)
• Fahrzeugprofil-Info (Vehicle profile information)
In the data area, the so-called active condition is displayed for each function group, as well as the
respective functions. Within the functions, the delivery values and/or parameters are visible if
selected in the upper filter area.
These values cannot be edited, they are displayed slightly greyed out. The values read out can be
edited, for this purpose the function Edit is available in the context menu.
Editing functional data
The values selected for editing appear in the area below and can be edited as text. Once editing is
complete, the changes can be applied using the button to the right above the values.
Changes are saved via the File/Save or Save As menu. It is also possible to save an FWL file in the
File menu. The symbol in the toolbar can also be used for saving.
Saving function data
193
When the file is saved after editing, the NCD is automatically signed. Here, the access data for the
SWL-Security Backend (see secure coding) and the BTLD number can be given.
NCD save, setting the bootloader number
NCD signing for Coding 2 or Coding 3 is only possible if the coding check stamp (CPS) in the NCD file
is valid.
18.8. View log files
E-Sys logs a variety of program events during execution, e.g. loading processes, flash processes and
much more. These logs are saved as so-called log files and can normally be found in the logs
subdirectory under the Data directory.
These files are a useful tool for analyzing error conditions or unexpected program states.
The files can be viewed directly in E-Sys using the Log Viewer module under Editors & Viewers.
Overview log viewer
194
E-Sys displays the contents of the logs directory in the E-Sys Data directory in the tree structure
under "E-Sys Logs".
 E-Sys cannot display the log file that is currently being written by E-Sys.
E-Sys continuously writes a new log file every time the program is started. However, this can only
be read as soon as E-Sys is either restarted or when a new log is started in E-Sys.
To start a new log in the log viewer, the (right) document symbol in the following figure should be
used. This will update the tree view directly. In other modules, the always visible icon highlighted
on the left in the illustration can be used to create a new log.
Start new log
18.8.1. Define separate log directory
If necessary, a separate log directory can be inserted into the tree view. This is done via the menu
195
item New in the context menu.
Set up working directory
These parameters are defined in the following dialog:
• (Display) name for the working directory
• File path to the display directory, via direct input or dialog-guided via the "…" button. button
• Extension: The file extension to be filtered for in the log directory. This is normally *.log
Define log directory
After confirming the dialog with OK, the working directory is mounted in the editor tree and the
available files become visible.
18.8.2. View Log Files / Tools
After double-clicking on a log file, the content is displayed on the right-hand side.
It is also possible to open the file in an external editor via the context menu (right-click on file, then
Open in Editor). To do this, an external editor program must be set in the main menu Options/
Settings. In addition, the log file must be loaded beforehand with a double click.
Setting the external editor
196
After opening a log file, further options are available in the context menu in the right-hand display
area. For example, the file can be saved after changes.
In addition, a search function is available which, after entering a search term, highlights all hits
found.

18.9.5. Timing
In the Timing tab the timing sequence is displayed. If the executed tal is loaded for the first time in
the viewer, a jpg file is generated and displayed. If the jpg file is already in the same directory as the
executed tal, it is displayed only. With the mouse wheel one can zoom the picture.
Sorting
The Timing tab can be sorted either by start time or by bus.
Sorted by start time
Sorted by bus
201
202
Chapter 19. Login at BMW backends
Some E-Sys operations require that the user authenticates first into the related BMW Backend. This
is the case for certificate management, signing coding data, retrieving Service29 certificates, and
more.
The following sections describe the login process at different backends.
19.1. Login to SWL Security System
Signing of net coding data for ECUs from SP2021 using productive keys must be done in a backend
for security reasons. For this purpose, the E-Sys user must both be activated in the backend
(SWLDevLic application via SWL-SEC2 in the B2B portal) and establish a connection to the backend.
The dialog for logging in can be called up using the button "Login" located in the status bar.
Login button
The user can choose between two different access points (BMW intranet / Internet), which can be
selected via the drop-down menu.
BASIC (username/password) and certificate-based authentication are supported as authentication
methods.
 If you choose BMW-Intranet your computer must be in the BMW IT-network.
Login to SWL Security System
19.2. Login to Sec4Diag
This login permits to fetch a session Id that allows to make protected requests to Sec4Diag backend
(e.g. getCertReqProfiles, getCertificates, etc.), by adding the session id to the Authorization header.
By clicking the tab “Sec4Diag Session Token” we have the login button and the state of the existing
203
session token:
Sec4Diag token not valid
The user will be asked for a strong authentication with username, pin and yubikey.
If successful, the expiration date will appear, and the token will be valid for future calls to the
backend:
Sec4Diag token valid
19.3. Login to SwlCockpit WEN (OIDC)
The process to login into SWL Cockpit is similar to the login to the Sec4Diag backend. The difference
is that in this case we are fetching a WEN token and will also see the expiration date:
204
SWL Cockpit login
19.4. SFA
Login to the backend to retrieve SFA tokens is available on the BMW Intranet only, using a
combination of CERTIFICATE+WEN:
Login to SFA
205
Chapter 20. Batch mode
This chapter describes batch mode functionality of E-Sys.
20.1. General information on batch operation
In addition to GUI mode, E-Sys can also be run in batch mode. For this purpose, the file E-Sys.bat
with various parameters is started in the E-Sys installation directory (default: C:\EC\Apps\ESG\ESys). Depending on the specified parameter, an appropriate action is performed.
In addition, 2 operating modes are available to the user in batch mode: client batch mode and
client-server batch mode.
What is client operation?
In client mode, the following steps are always followed during TAL processing in batch mode:
1. Start E-Sys batch instance
2. Establish connection to vehicle
3. Execute TAL
4. Close connection to vehicle
5. Close E-Sys-Batch Instance
If you want to execute multiple TALs with the same vehicle connection, opening and closing the
vehicle connection and starting and stopping an E-Sys batch instance means unnecessary overhead.
On the production-line, fast coding times are required, so a client-server-based batch mode has
been introduced.
Thus, it is possible to start an E-Sys server instance, which is controlled with the help of a client.
In this way, individual E-Sys functions can be offered in batch.
How client-server batch mode works:
An E-Sys batch server is started, waiting for client requests. To check if an E-Sys batch server is
running, the -check command is offered (see Server-client batch mode).
A client can be started by specifying the commands with the batch parameter -server in another
command line window (see General overview of commands).
The client connects to a running E-Sys batch server, transfers the parameters specified on the
command line to the server, and waits for a response.
The server performs the appropriate action and reports the result to the client. The client then exits
with the appropriate return value.
The E-Sys batch server runs until it exits.
206
Example of a server-client operation:
1. Start E-Sys batch instance
2. Establish connection to vehicle
3. Read SVT
4. Close connection to vehicle
5. Import PDX Container
6. Establish connection to vehicle
7. Calculate TAL
8. Execute TAL
9. Close connection to vehicle
10. Read SVT
11. Close E-Sys-Batch Instance
Outputs to the console
When an action is written to the console, messages are output to the client console.
Logging
The log behavior can be set in the E-Sys.properties.
Default behavior: (log.file.client = false or not present in E-Sys.properties)
The client does not create a log file. This is not necessary because the client is only used to start an
action on the server.
This means that the complete business logic runs on the server and is also logged there.
Log-File Splitting in Server Client Mode: (log.file.client = true in E-Sys.properties)
This setting creates a new log file for each client request for the server and client.
The file name shows which client request is involved.
Examples:
• E-Sys_20160203_150924_client_openconnection.log
• E-Sys_20160203_150924_server_openconnection.log
• E-Sys_20160203_151145_client_closeconnection.log
• E-Sys_20160203_151145_server_closeconnection.log
Client-Server Connection
A TCP connection is established between the client and the server via port 30303.
207
If the port is not available, another port can be configured in the E-Sys.properties file
(BatchServer.port, -prop <E-Sys.properties>).
 Connections between client and server go through "localhost", i.e. the client and server must always
 be started on the same machine.
Relative Paths
Batch can use relative paths in addition with absolute paths.
This feature is configured in the E-Sys properties files via the line Path.Batch=. Only the properties
file needs to be defined using absolute path.
Example:
Path.Batch=C:\Users\User\Documents\
Restrictions
Only one E-Sys instance can run on a computer at a time.
This means that either the GUI mode, the E-Sys client or the E-Sys batch server must be started.
Only one client can be connected to the server at a time.
 Note: TAL processing in client-server batch mode:
While the client that started the TAL processing is still waiting for the result, another client can
request a cancellation of the TAL processing.

20.3. Anflash
The Anflash module offers the possibility to perform a complete flash cycle in a fully automated
way.
To start the Anflash process in batch mode, a master config file is given as a parameter to the
following command. The master config file must be specified with its absolute path.
Optionally, the parameter -ignoreBATHAF can be passed to the command.
The exact structure of the required configuration files is described in the Anflash manual.
Batch-command Anflash
220
Legend:
• [] optional, can be specified, but does not have to
• () selection, must be specified
• | "or", is used in a selection
Command in client batch mode:
E-Sys.bat -anflash <config file> [-ignoreBATHAF]
Command in client-server batch mode:
E-Sys.bat -server -anflash <config file> [-ignoreBATHAF]
Declaration:
-anflash <config file> Absolute path to Anflash-Configuration-file (see
anflash).
-ignoreBATHAF Optional parameter. Ignores the S1-switch.
Example:
E-Sys.bat -anflash C:\data\executeAnflash.config -ignoreBATHAF
Information:
• Information about the batch command -anflash is to be obtained from the anflash manual.
• If a BAT/HAF test reveals that switch S1 is open, the further execution of the command depends
on parameter -ignoreBATHAF.
◦ -ignoreBATHAF has been set: The flash sequence continues. However, the user must be aware
that the execution can lead to interruptions. In this case, the TAL-processing cannot be
ended with value 0 (OK), but at best with value 4 (with warning).
◦ -ignoreBATHAF not set: The execution of the command -talexecution is canceled.
• The following codes are returned:
◦ 0 - The action was successful.
◦ 1 - An exception occurred so the action could not be completed.
◦ 2 - The action was performed with errors.
◦ 3 - Unable to connect to the server.
◦ 4 - The action was performed without errors but with warnings.
◦ 5 - The action was not processed.
◦ 6 - The action was aborted by the user.
221
20.3.1. Check failed
If the switch S1 is open, then the further procedure depends on whether the parameter
-ignoreBATHAF was set when the command -anflash was called or not.
-ignoreBATHAF set
The flash process is continued. However, the user must be aware that aborts may occur during the
execution of the flash process. In this case, the TAL execution cannot be terminated with the value 0
(OK), but at best with the value 4 (with warning).
-ignoreBATHAF not set
The execution of the command anflash is canceled.
20.3.2. Connection parameters
To establish a connection please check the batch section: Connection parameter

Backend authentication for Coding
Log in to the Coding-Backend (necessary to sign the NCDs)
Command in client batch mode:
---only applicable in server-client operation---

<username>\|-useSwlSecCertificate) [-dialog]
Declaration:
222
-authenticationCoding command.

max.mustermann).

Information:

Certificate-based authentication can be specified.

The Login dialog looks like this:
Login dialog
• For Certificate-based authentication, the required client Certificate must first be imported using
the -importSwlSecCertificate batch command or in GUI mode.

the E-Sys client or E-Sys server.
223
Basic authentication displays both the authorization and the expiration date of the
authorization.
In the case of successful Certificate-based authentication, the quota and the Certificate’s usage
time are also displayed.
